Kentucky Division of Water Provides Guidance on Emergency Water Disinfection
Targeted News Service
May 4, 2010 Tuesday 12:58 AM EST


Copyright 2010 Targeted News Service LLC All Rights Reserved
Length: 524 words
Byline: Targeted News Service
Dateline: FRANKFORT, Ky.
Body


The Kentucky Environmental and Public Protection Cabinet issued the following news release:
As power outages, low water pressure problems and flood conditions persist in some areas of the commonwealth following last weekend's storms, the Kentucky Division of Water urges residents to properly disinfect water for in-home use, including drinking, cooking, making prepared drinks and brushing teeth.
The easiest alternative is to use bottled water if it is available and has not been exposed to flood waters.
In the absence of safe bottled water, tap water should be boiled to kill most types of disease-causing organisms that may be present. If the water is cloudy, filter it through clean cloths or coffee filters or allow it to settle. Afterwards, draw off the clear water and boil for one minute. The cooled water may be stored in clean containers with covers.
If you are unable to boil water, you can disinfect it using household bleach that contains 5.25 percent sodium hypochlorite. Chlorine bleach will kill some, but not all, types of disease-causing organisms that may be in the water. Do not use scented bleaches, color-safe bleaches or bleaches with added cleaners. If the water is cloudy, filter it and use the clear water for disinfection. Add one-eighth teaspoon (or eight drops) of regular, unscented, liquid household chlorine bleach for each gallon of water (one teaspoon of bleach disinfects five gallons of water). Stir it well and let it stand for 30 minutes before use. Store the disinfected water in clean containers with covers.
Since liquid chlorine bleach loses strength over time, only fresh bleach should be used for water disinfection. For bleach that is one to two years old, the dosage should be doubled.
Another method of disinfection is to use common household iodine from the medicine chest or first-aid kit. Add five drops of 2 percent U.S. tincture of iodine to each quart or liter of clear water. For cloudy water, add ten drops and let the solution stand for at least 30 minutes.
Additional tips:
* To improve the taste or boiled or bleached-treated water, allow it to stand for several hours or aerate it by pouring from one clean container to another several times. A pinch of salt added per quart or liter will also improve the flat taste.
* Do not consume iodine-treated water if you are pregnant, iodine-sensitive or have a history of thyroid disease.
* Use bottled or boiled water for preparing powdered or concentrated infant formulas.
* Boil all tap water used for washing raw vegetables and fruit.
* Wash dishes in sink full of tap water to which one tablespoon of household bleach has been added. Air-dry the dishes before use.
* Use treated water for teeth brushing since swallowing could occur.
* Bathe or shower in untreated water but avoid contact with the mouth and eyes. Infants and toddlers should be sponge-bathed. No special soaps are necessary.
* See your family physician or healthcare provider if you become sick.
* Continue to treat water until health officials remove the boil water advisory.
Contact: Allison Fleck, 502/564-3410

WATERBORNE ILLNESSES, STRONG CURRENTS POSE RISK OF HARM
States News Service
May 4, 2010 Tuesday


Copyright 2010 States News Service
Length: 545 words
Byline: States News Service
Dateline: NASHVILLE, TN
Body


The following information was released by the Tennessee Emergency Management Agency:
When floods occur, affected residents run the risk of contracting waterborne illnesses caused by bacteria, viruses, chemicals or toxins found in the water. People can be exposed by ingesting, breathing in, or simply contacting contaminated water. Additionally, walking, wading or even playing in flood waters might pose a potential hazard of drowning. Avoiding flood waters whenever possible is the best strategy to prevent illness and injury.
Waterborne illnesses and flood related injuries pose a serious risk to residents affected by this natural disaster, said State Health Commissioner Susan R. Cooper, MSN, RN. Parents should take extra precaution by keeping children and teens out of potentially contaminated flood waters. While it might not be obvious, currents can be strong and pose an immediate potential for drowning. Protect your loved ones and keep them safe by staying away from flood water.
Overtaxed and flooded septic and municipal wastewater systems will occasionally contaminate flood waters, increasing the risk of disease transmission. When there is risk of drinking water contamination, a boil water advisory will issued to help protect the health of a community and should be taken very seriously. These advisories tell residents how to boil or disinfect their tap water for use. For more instructions regarding drinking water advisories, visit the Web at http://www.epa.gov/safewater/faq/emerg.html. To see a list of water systems that have issued boil notices, see the Web at   http://www.tennessee.gov/environment/flood/.
Fast moving water and even shallow, standing water can pose dangers. Regardless of your ability to swim, as little as a few inches of water can cause drowning. Also, flood-related injuries or wounds can occur from contact with sharp objects such as glass or metal fragments, leading to infection that may require medical attention.
It is important to remember that during a disaster situation, personal hygiene and sanitation are critical to help prevent the spread of disease. If you must be in contact with flood water, take necessary precautions and wash thoroughly with soap and clean water afterward. Make sure to keep hands clean, which helps prevent the spread of germs. Always wash your hands with soap and clean water. Use water from an approved source or that has been boiled or disinfected. If water is not available, alcohol-based hand sanitizers can be used. People should wash their hands:
before and after preparing and eating food.
after using the toilet.
after changing diapers or cleaning up a child who has used the toilet.
before and after tending to someone who is sick.
after blowing your nose, coughing or sneezing.
after handling an animal, animal waste or garbage.
before and after treating a cut or wound.
If running water is not available, a temporary hand-washing station can be created using a large water spigot jug that contains water from an approved source. If being used indoors, use a catch basin to catch the water. Also have soap, paper towels and a trash can available.
For a complete list of natural disasters and how to prepare and respond to them, please visit CDC's Web site at http://www.bt.cdc.gov/DISASTERS/.

Load-Date: May 5, 2010
END OF DOCUMENT

BOIL WATER ADVISORY RESCINDED FOR CITY OF SCAMMON
States News Service
May 5, 2010 Wednesday


Copyright 2010 States News Service
Length: 153 words
Byline: States News Service
Dateline: TOPEKA, KS
Body


The following information was released by the Kansas Department of Health and Environment:
The Kansas Department of Health and Environment (KDHE) has rescinded a boil water advisory for the city of Scammon, which is located in Cherokee County. The boil water advisory issued for the City of Roseland still remains in effect.
KDHE issued the advisory for both cities on May 3 due to a break in the water main that resulted in a loss of pressure to the water distribution system. Laboratory testing on samples collected in Scammon indicates no evidence of contamination, and all other conditions that place the system at risk of contamination are deemed by KDHE officials to be resolved. One sample collected from Roseland tested positive for coliform bacteria. Additional samples will be collected from Roseland.
The city and/or KDHE will notify media when the boil water advisory has been rescinded for the City of Roseland.

Environment Department Lifts 'Boil Water Advisory' for Turquoise Trail Elementary School
Targeted News Service
May 6, 2010 Thursday 12:51 AM EST


Copyright 2010 Targeted News Service LLC All Rights Reserved
Length: 227 words
Byline: Targeted News Service
Dateline: SANTA FE, N.M.
Body


The New Mexico Department of the Environment issued the following news release:
The New Mexico Environment Department's Drinking Water Bureau is lifting a "boil water advisory" for the Turquoise Trail Elementary School.
NMED issued the advisory on April 29, 2010 after bacteriological contamination that exceeded the Maximum Contaminant Level for E. coli was discovered in drinking water at the school. NMED required the Turquoise Trail Elementary School to notify all water consumers of the finding.
Corrective actions were taken by the water system, including disinfecting the water system by increasing the level of chlorination and identifying possible sources of contamination. Consumers were advised to boil all water prior to ingestion.
Water samples collected since the corrective actions were taken have shown no E. coli present in the water system. These clean results have allowed NMED's Drinking Water Bureau to advise Turquoise Trail Elementary School to lift the "boil water advisory" for the water system.
For more information, call NMED Communications Director Marissa Stone Bardino at (505) 827-0314 or (505) 231-0475 or Mike Huber, Drinking Water Bureau Compliance Manager, at (505) 476-8638.

DAMAGE ASSESSMENTS BEGIN ACROSS COMMONWEALTH
States News Service
May 7, 2010 Friday


Copyright 2010 States News Service
Length: 773 words
Byline: States News Service
Dateline: FRANKFORT, Ky.
Body


The following information was released by the office of the governor of Kentucky:
Federal emergency teams joined local and state officials in several counties today to begin estimating damages from last weekend's devastating storms and flooding.
Federal Emergency Management Agency (FEMA) personnel arrived in Frankfort yesterday for briefings with the Kentucky Division of Emergency Management (KyEM) officials. County damage assessments began this morning.
These assessments are a critical part of the process to organize recovery and for getting the federal assistance we need, said Governor Steve Beshear. I strongly encourage citizens to cooperate with the teams. Canvassing our state to estimate the extensive damage will be an arduous task, and I appreciate the efforts of FEMA and our local emergency officials.
FEMA assessors visited affected counties with personnel from local emergency management, local elected officials, KyEM, Kentucky Transportation Cabinet, Kentucky Department of Public Health and the Kentucky National Guard. As each county assessment is completed, teams will be reassigned to new counties and work will continue over the weekend. Teams will review the storms' impact on both government property and individual citizens.
This is a complicated task, the scope and widespread damage is creating a challenge for us to get to all the impacted counties at once, said John Heltzel, director of the KyEM. Let me assure you; if you have not seen these teams in your counties, you will.
Officials encourage those who have suffered property damage to photograph the damage, save any repair receipts and report damage to the local emergency management director.
Monitoring Lake Levels
Emergency personnel continue to watch the basin of the lower Ohio River and lake levels and continue working closely with local, state and federal officials to prepare for flooding as a result of the high waters.
Residents should be aware that lake releases are necessary to guard against damaging the dams and to control lake levels.
KyEM, the Kentucky Division of Water and United States Army Corps of Engineers, as well as other state and local emergency officials, continue to monitor water levels behind all dams and levees across the Commonwealth.
Residents can get more information about rising waters by visiting the KyEM website at www.kyem.ky.gov or the USACE at   www.lrl.usace.army.mil.
Body of Kayaker Recovered
The Hart County coroner has confirmed the recovery of the body of a missing kayaker who disappeared in the Green River earlier this week. This brings the fatality count to five deaths associated with this storm.
I am saddened by the news of another fatality due to the storm, and my thoughts are with the friends and family, said Gov. Beshear. This latest loss of life is a reminder that people must avoid entering floodwaters they are swift and dangerous.
Pulaski County officials continue to search for a missing 18-year-old kayaker.
Storm Numbers:
79 counties and 36 cities have declared States of Emergency
5 confirmed fatalities
Nearly 80 National Guard soldiers are on the ground assisting local officials
25 boil water advisories (BWA) affecting approximately 83,000 Kentuckians
500 well disinfection kits prepared for distribution
Turn Around, Don't Drown
Do not drive through or wade through any water, no matter if it's just a few inches. Stop, turn around - don't drown. Do not venture onto flooded waterways for recreation. If you must travel by boat, for whatever reason, wear a personal flotation device.
Water Safety
The Kentucky Division of Water reports that, while most drinking water systems are up and running, boil water advisories are in effect for some areas due to broken lines and other factors. Check with your local government or public works officials for current boil water advisory status.
The division also warns against contact with floodwaters due to contamination from sewage, agricultural products and other harmful substances.
Citizens should be advised that water contaminated in one part of the state travels through fast-flowing rivers and streams to other areas, causing widespread bacterial contamination. If you should come into contact with floodwater, immediately wash the affected areas with hot water and antibacterial soap.
Road Repairs
More roads are reopening as conditions improve. Highway crews are continuing to repair pavement breaks, culvert failures, embankment erosion, guardrail and other flood-related damage statewide. For a list of road closings, and conditions, across the Commonwealth, visit www.511.ky.gov
For additional information, visit the KyEM website at www.kyem.ky.gov.

OHIO
House fire kills girl, 1, in eastern Ohio
A fire that apparently spread quickly through a house in eastern Ohio has killed a 1-year-old girl.
The Jefferson County coroner's office says Savannah Creamer died in the fire in the house near Mingo Junction around 9:30 a.m. Sunday.
Jefferson County Sheriff Fred Abdalla said he has reason to believe a 4-year-old in the house might have been playing with matches before the fire. Sheriff Abdalla said the 4-year-old came out of a bathroom and said there was a fire. He said the investigation is continuing.
Deborah Welsch, the coroner's office chief investigator, says it appears the 1-year-old girl died of smoke inhalation after becoming trapped in the house.
Ms. Welsch says the girl's parents and six other children got out of the house, but two children were injured when they fell or jumped out of windows. Sheriff Abdalla said one of the children who fell or jumped was taken to a Pittsburgh hospital.
Ms. Welsch says the initial call referred to a room on fire, but firefighters arrived to find the entire house ablaze.
ALLEGHENY COUNTY
Most power restored after Saturday's winds
Overnight restoration work reduced the impact of Saturday's power outages that were caused by high winds that tore through the region.
As of 6 p.m. Sunday, Duquesne Light was reporting that 150 customers were still without service, down from a peak of 9,200 Saturday afternoon.
Allegheny Energy reported that service was restored to virtually all customers in Pennsylvania as of Sunday evening, down from about 13,000 in Pennsylvania on Saturday.
Throughout the company's four-state territory, some 35,000 customers were without service Saturday and all but 160 were restored as of Sunday evening, said spokesman Jeffrey Straight. Outages were widespread, he said, but were concentrated Saturday in Pittsburgh and New Stanton.
Duquesne Light outages were concentrated in Penn Hills, Baldwin, West Mifflin, Aleppo, Hampton, Leet, Moon, Ross and Shaler.
CITY
Police arrest suspect in Homewood slaying
A Homewood man was arrested Sunday and charge with fatally shooting an East Liberty man early Saturday inside a home on North Murtland Avenue in Homewood, police said.
Virgil Williams 34, has been charged with homicide in the killing of Michael Garnett Jr., 19, who was shot at 2:40 a.m. Saturday and was pronounced dead at 8:14 a.m. at UPMC Presbyterian.
Mr. Williams is in the Allegheny County Jail and faces a hearing May 14, police said.
Point Park U. gets gift, matching grant
The Richard King Mellon Foundation has donated $2 million outright to Point Park University's new student and convocation center and pledged a $2 million matching award toward the project, the university said Thursday.
To receive the full $2 million match, Point Park will have to raise $2 million of its own through donations, university spokeswoman Mary Ellen Solomon said. She declined to say how much Point Park has thus far raised.
If the $2 million match is triggered in full, it, combined with the $2 million foundation grant in hand, would constitute the largest gift by an individual or foundation in Point Park's history. The money will help the university of nearly 4,000 students establish its center in the former YMCA building at 330 Blvd. of the Allies, Downtown.
"The Student and Convocation Center will become the hub of our campus and student activities," Point Park President Paul Hennigan said in a statement. "The support of the Richard King Mellon Foundation is critical to our success in providing academic and recreational spaces for our students and an amenity for the Downtown community."
Group hopes to build memorial to fallen officers
A group raising money to build a permanent memorial to three slain Pittsburgh police officers hopes to win a $50,000 grant through the Pepsi soft drink company with the help of online voters.
The Bloomfield Development Corp. needs about that much money to complete a $116,000 statue and memorial garden outside St. Joseph Church on Liberty Avenue to honor fallen Officers Paul J. Sciullo II, Eric G. Kelly, and Stephen Mayhle.
"It's just a matter of everybody voting," said Executive Director Karla Owens. "It's a really great program."
Pepsi awards grants based on how many votes a project receives online. The competition is nationwide and voting continues through May at www.refresheverything.com. The project's title is "I want to build a memorial garden for fallen police officers."
SOUTH
Water main broken in Mt. Lebanon
A water main break in Mt. Lebanon disrupted service to about 50 customers when a private plumbing contractor broke an eight-inch main line Sunday, said Josephine Posti, a spokeswoman for Pennsylvania American Water. The main is located on Pinewood Drive.
Initially, it was feared that about 10 homes had sustained some level of damage but Ms. Posti said it appeared Sunday that only one or two homes were impacted by the break.
Emergency responders were called at 9:30 a.m. and cleared the scene within an hour, according to an emergency dispatch supervisor.
Ms. Posti said the break was repaired Sunday afternoon but a boil-water advisory remains in effect for affected customers.

Mount Joy Issues Boil Water Alert
Intelligencer Journal/New Era (Lancaster, Pennsylvania)
May 12, 2010 Wednesday


Copyright 2010 Lancaster Newspapers, Inc.
Section: B; Pg. 6
Length: 306 words
Byline: Civia Katz, Correspondent
Dateline: Lancaster, PA
Body


BY CIVIA KATZ
Correspondent
Mount Joy Borough water customers were alerted to boil water Monday night after a contractor damaged a water main pipe that runs across the Chiques Creek.
The alert came from the borough water authority's emergency phone system, which was used for the first time in the emergency.
The Swift Reach Network was able to contact residents within 15 minutes of the break.
Terry Kauffman, borough special projects manager, said Tuesday that 33 residential units were affected, but at one point every customer was without water. About six properties were without water for several hours.
The water system lost pressure and, under state Department of Environmental Protection policy, the municipality was required to issue a boil water alert. The danger is that the water can become contaminated with bacteria such as E. coli.
The borough conducted the first bacterial test on Tuesday for possible contamination and is waiting for lab results. A second test will be done Thursday. If both tests are negative, the boil water advisory can be lifted.
"We need to do the precautionary tests to see that it is OK before we can tell (residents) it's OK to drink. That's established by the DEP," Kauffman said.
More precaution is needed with this break because of its proximity to the Chiques Creek. It is a trout stream, and the borough has to avoid contamination.
"The contractor hit a little pipe that crossed the Chiques Creek near Manheim Road. It went back to the 1940s, not on any maps. No one knew it was there," Kauffman said. "You try to keep track of them but no one knew. I really can't say anyone is at fault."
The borough has dug a hole by the stream and is pumping it out to keep the water from draining into the creek.
When the boil water ban is lifted, the borough will again notify the public using the direct call system.

Markey: Our Country's Aging Water Infrastructure Needs An Upgrade
Targeted News Service
May 13, 2010 Thursday 5:46 AM EST


Copyright 2010 Targeted News Service LLC All Rights Reserved
Length: 759 words
Byline: Targeted News Service
Dateline: WASHINGTON
Body


Rep. Edward J. Markey, D-Mass. (7th CD), issued the following news release:
Representative Edward J. Markey (D-Mass.), chairman of the Energy and Environment Subcommittee of the Energy and Commerce Committee today released the following prepared remarks at a hearing on the Assistance, Quality and Affordability Act of 2010:
"When people turn on their bathroom or kitchen faucets they often take for granted that an abundant supply of clean water flows freely from their taps. It is only when the water stops flowing due to a catastrophic failure that attention is given to the complexities of providing clean, safe drinking water.
"A prime example of such a catastrophic failure occurred just over a week ago in Massachusetts, when a breach in a seven year old pipe caused a water supply emergency that affected over 2 million residents of Boston and its surrounding areas, including a large portion of my district.
"A boil-water advisory lasted for several days. People swarmed the Stop and Shop and other grocery stores to stock up on bottled water. Restaurants and diners had to close because they had no water to serve or wash dishes with. And people had to get through Monday without their morning cup of Dunkin' Donuts-which resulted in a near riot at the Dunkin' Donuts across from my District Office in Medford Square. In the Boston papers, the entire incident became know as the Aqua-pocalypse.
"Although the MWRA incident could not have been anticipated because the pipe that broke was so new, public attention immediately turned to the need for increased federal funding for infrastructure projects that ensure a safe drinking water supply for years to come.
"The reality is that the country's drinking water infrastructure is rapidly aging. EPA estimates that over the next 20 years, water systems will need to invest nearly $335 billion dollars on infrastructure improvements to ensure safe water to our nation. Water systems simply can't afford to do this on their own, and people who are already struggling to pay their water bills can't absorb these costs either. We cannot turn off the flow of federal funding for this essential infrastructure at a time when our water systems need it most.
"The Assistance, Quality, and Affordability Act that Chairman Waxman and I have introduced will reauthorize the Safe Drinking Water Act State Revolving Fund for the first time since its creation in 1996 and will make a number of changes to invest in our future.
"The bill increases water project funding from $1.5 billion dollars in 2011 to $6 billion dollars in 2015. This will mean that more drinking water projects can be completed, and that more jobs are created for people who need them. A December 2008 report from the U.S. Conference of Mayors estimated that every million dollars of drinking water and wastewater infrastructure investment directly creates 8.7 jobs. Over the next 5 years, our legislation would therefore lead to more than 100,000 new jobs.
"We have also included a new emphasis on cutting-edge projects to allow funding priority to be granted for projects that will make drinking water safe and affordable for years to come. We will also encourage projects that increase water and energy efficiency, and projects that anticipate future problems and propose repairs before a crisis occurs.
"We've ensured that we are directing resources to those who need it most, so that water systems serving communities that can't afford to pay for the upgrades necessary to comply with Safe Drinking Water Act standards are given what they need to do so.
"We've also included a change in drinking water enforcement requirements that will ensure that systems that have violated drinking water standards in the past are inspected to ensure they stay compliant. I would like to thank Congressman Bobby Rush for his work in this area, following a truly horrific case in the village of Crestwood, Illinois in which people were literally and knowingly poisoned by the water they were drinking for decades.
"Finally, this bill also includes my language to strengthen EPA's endocrine disruptor screening program. Endocrine disrupting chemicals are like computer viruses that, over time, can severely disrupt your body's operating system, and it is vital that EPA have a more robust and transparent program that screens drinking water contaminants to identify the chemicals that pose such concerns.
"I thank the witnesses for attending today's hearing. We look forward to your testimony."
Copyright Targeted News Services
TNS MJ88-JF78-100514-2805025 StaffFurigay

Boil water advisory for southern Jefferson County
The Associated Press State & Local Wire
May 17, 2010 Monday 11:02 AM GMT


Copyright 2010 Associated Press All Rights Reserved
Section: STATE AND REGIONAL
Length: 88 words
Dateline: LOUISVILLE Ky.
Body


The Louisville Water Company has issued a boil water advisory for about 1,000 customers in southern Jefferson County.
A news release Monday morning stated the advisory is a precaution after pressure dropped in two elevated storage tanks.
The utility advised affected customers to boil all water used for drinking and cooking for three minutes.
Those customers also should not use chilled water from refrigerators or ice dispensers.
The affected area is within a boundary of East Pages Lane, St. Andrews Church Road and Third Street Road.

START OF DOCUMENT







Boil Advisory Issued for Swea City
Targeted News Service
May 21, 2010 Friday 5:53 AM EST


Copyright 2010 Targeted News Service LLC All Rights Reserved
Length: 237 words
Byline: Targeted News Service
Dateline: SWEA CITY, Iowa
Body


The Iowa Department of Natural Resources issued the following news release:
A major water main break at Swea City in Kossuth County has prompted a boil advisory for that community.
The water main break resulted in the entire tower draining Thursday night. Since there is no water pressure in the system until the repairs can be made, a boil advisory is in effect until the system is restored and the necessary testing can take place to make sure the water is safe. It is anticipated that water pressure could be restored today, but the boil advisory will remain in affect until the entire system can be chlorinated, flush and tested to ensure there is no bacterial contamination in the system.
The city is working on arrangements to provide bottled water to residents until all of the repairs and testing have occurred.
It is recommended not to drink the water without boiling it first. Bring all water to a boil, let it boil for one minute, and let it cool before using, or use bottled water. Boiled or bottled water should be used for drinking, making ice, brushing teeth, and food preparation until further notice. Boiling kills bacteria and other organisms in the water. The water may be used for bathing and other similar purposes. More information on disinfecting water is available on the EPA Safe Drinking Water Hotline at (800) 426-4791.
Copyright Targeted News Services

WALLA WALLA COUNTY: BOIL-WATER ADVISORY ISSUED FOR GREEN TANK DISTRICT
States News Service
June 9, 2010 Wednesday


Copyright 2010 States News Service
Length: 257 words
Byline: States News Service
Dateline: OLYMPIA, WA
Body


The following information was released by the Washington State Department of Health:
The state Department of Health and the Green Tank Irrigation District 11 advise residents served by Green Tank to boil their tap water or buy bottled water until further notice. Potentially harmful bacteria have been detected in the water system.
The advisory affects about 170 homes and businesses served by Green Tank. The district's service area is generally north of College Place and west of Walla Walla (http://wallawallagis.com/PDFS/MAPS/WATER_SERVICE_AREAS/GREEN%20TANK%20IRRIGATION%20DISTRICT.pdf).
E. coli was detected in routine water samples. The state health Office of Drinking Water is working closely with the water system's operator to pinpoint the source of contamination and fix the problem. It may be tied to pump failures that occurred last week.
The health advisory includes several precautionary steps customers should take. Use boiled water or bottled water for drinking, brushing teeth, preparing food, dishwashing, and making ice. Tap water should be boiled for one minute and allowed to cool before use.
While there have been no reports of illness associated with this contamination event, the advisory will remain in effect until the water system operator and the state health agency are satisfied there is no longer a health threat to the system's customers.
Customers who have questions should call Green Tank Irrigation District at 509-525-4608, or Walla Walla County Health District (Barry Jenkins or Jeanette Lightfoot) at 509-524-2662.

Load-Date: June 10, 2010
END OF DOCUMENT

"Precautionary Boil Water Advisory" door signs were placed on the businesses/residences so as to inform the customers of this situation and to provide contact information. Larger signs were placed at specific intersections within the service area.
Therefore, as a precaution, we advise that all water used for drinking, cooking, making ice, brushing teeth, or washing dishes be boiled. A rolling boil of one minute is sufficient. As an alternative bottled water may be used.
This "Precautionary Boil Water Notice" will remain in effect until the problem has been corrected and bacteriological survey shows that the water is safe to drink.
If you have any questions you may contact Seminole County Environmental Services Department at 407.665.2110 between the hours of 8:00am - 5:00 pm, Monday through Friday, or call 407.665.2767 all other hours.

Muhlenberg Co. testing new warning system
The Associated Press State & Local Wire
June 12, 2010 Saturday 5:11 PM GMT


Copyright 2010 Associated Press All Rights Reserved
Section: STATE AND REGIONAL
Length: 147 words
Dateline: OWENSBORO Ky.
Body


A new warning system in Muhlenberg County would contact residents by home phone, cell phone, text message and e-mails about bad weather or other potential problems.
The county's fiscal court voted Thursday to adopt the system for a trial year at a cost of $22,500.
Judge-Executive Rick Newman told the Owensboro Messenger-Inquirer that given recent disasters like the January 2009 ice storm and a tornado in February 2008, they felt like it was worth trying out the system.
CodeRED, a Louisville company, supplies the warning system, which Newman said should be operational by Aug. 1.
Central City Mayor Barry Shaver said the system could help to alert people during the night or can be specific to certain sections of the city and county, which would be helpful during power outages or boil water advisories.
Information from: Owensboro Messenger-Inquirer, http://www.messenger-inquirer.com

Load-Date: June 13, 2010
END OF DOCUMENT


START OF DOCUMENT







BOIL, WATER CONSERVATION ADVISORY ISSUED FOR CITY OF ADAIR
States News Service
June 14, 2010 Monday


Copyright 2010 States News Service
Length: 219 words
Byline: States News Service
Dateline: ADAIR
Body


The following information was released by the Iowa Department of Natural Resources:
Residents of Adair are being advised to use only bottled water for consumption until a broken water main can be repaired.
An advisory to boil and conserve water was issued Sunday evening after a water main going from the city's well to its water treatment plant ruptured. However, since water is being brought in from surrounding communities in fire trucks, residents are being urged to use bottled water as extra precaution against potential water contamination.
Retailers within Adair are working with the county emergency management office to increase bottled water supplies until the advisory is lifted.
Residents are also being urged to conserve water usage as the city tries to maintain water pressure in its system utilizing the water being brought in from other communities.
Adair is attempting to locate the break and will be repairing the water main. After the repairs, the city will flush the lines and collect bacteria samples. Additional flushing may need to be conducted. This advisory is a precaution until bacterial sample results are available. The public will be notified when the results are available and the advisory is lifted.
Adair is working with the Iowa Department of Natural Resources to resolve the situation.

Load-Date: June 14, 2010
END OF DOCUMENT

Boil, Water Conservation Advisory Issued for City of Adair
Targeted News Service
June 14, 2010 Monday 5:44 AM EST


Copyright 2010 Targeted News Service LLC All Rights Reserved

Byline: Targeted News Service
Dateline: ADAIR, Iowa
Body


The Iowa Department of Natural Resources issued the following news release:
Residents of Adair are being advised to use only bottled water for consumption until a broken water main can be repaired.
An advisory to boil and conserve water was issued Sunday evening after a water main going from the city's well to its water treatment plant ruptured. However, since water is being brought in from surrounding communities in fire trucks, residents are being urged to use bottled water as extra precaution against potential water contamination.
Retailers within Adair are working with the county emergency management office to increase bottled water supplies until the advisory is lifted.
Residents are also being urged to conserve water usage as the city tries to maintain water pressure in its system utilizing the water being brought in from other communities.
Adair is attempting to locate the break and will be repairing the water main. After the repairs, the city will flush the lines and collect bacteria samples. Additional flushing may need to be conducted. This advisory is a precaution until bacterial sample results are available. The public will be notified when the results are available and the advisory is lifted.

IT'S TIME TO GET SAVVY ABOUT SODIUM
States News Service
June 14, 2010 Monday


Copyright 2010 States News Service
Length: 386 words
Byline: States News Service
Dateline: TOPEKA, KS
Body


The following information was released by the Kansas Department of Health and Environment:
The Kansas Department of Health and Environment (KDHE) and Saline County RWD #7 are issuing a boil water advisory for the water customers of the Saline County RWD #7 water system, located in southwest Saline County. Customers of Saline County RWD #1 are not affected by this advisory.
KDHE officials are issuing the advisory in advance of repairs that are scheduled to be made between 8:00 PM and 11:00 PM on Monday, June 14, 2010. During this time, a valve will be replaced which will cause an interruption of water service resulting in little or no water pressure. Whenever such a loss of pressure occurs, it is possible for contaminants to enter the system. Also during this time, disinfection (chlorine) levels are inadequate to protect against bacterial contamination.
Water customers should consider filling sanitary containers with tap water, or obtaining bottled water for consumption until the advisory has been lifted. When water service is restored, residents served by the affected public water systems should observe the following precautions:
Boil water vigorously for one minute prior to use. Boiling longer than three minutes may adversely affect the quality and taste of the water.
Use only boiled water for drinking, diluting fruit juices, and all other food preparation.
Dispose of ice cubes and do not use ice from a household automatic icemaker. Remake ice cubes with water that has been boiled.
Disinfect dishes and other food contact surfaces by immersion for at least one minute in clean tap water that contains one teaspoon of unscented household bleach per gallon of water.
Water used for bathing does not generally need to be boiled. Supervision of children is necessary while bathing or using backyard pools so water is not ingested. Persons with cuts or severe rashes may wish to consult their physicians.
Questions regarding the status of this advisory may be directed to Bruce Spare by calling (785) 667-6903. The advisory will remain in effect until testing of water samples indicates no evidence of contamination and all other conditions which place the systems at risk of contamination are deemed by KDHE officials to be resolved. KDHE will notify media when the boil water advisory has been rescinded.

Load-Date: June 16, 2010
END OF DOCUMENT

Algoma U Students: 'First Nations Water Bill is Leaky'
Targeted News Service
June 15, 2010 Tuesday 12:17 AM EST


Copyright 2010 Targeted News Service LLC All Rights Reserved
Length: 411 words
Byline: Targeted News Service
Dateline: SAULT STE. MARIE, Canada
Body


Algoma University issued the following news release:
Students at Algoma University have responded to the proposed First Nations Water Legislation (Bill S-11), saying that while the efforts are long overdue, it is a small step in the right direction, with more work needed for the bill to carry any long term viability.
"It's concerning that the bill will create legislation, but will fail to implement adequate skills training and resources to First Nations communities to meet the regulations" says Katie Yakasovich, Vice-President External of the Algoma University Students Union (AUSU). "It's also disheartening that the government would spend $1.9 Million to create a fake lake in Downtown Toronto, but will not invest in the health and sustainability of our communities."
AUSU, in solidarity with the Shingwauk Anishnaabe Students Association (SASA) continue to work towards enlightening the federal government on the issues with the over 120 First Nations communities that do not have access to clean drinking water.
Algoma U Graduate Joanne Robertson and supporters are actively working on the Empty Glass for Water campaign, to raise awareness with the Federal government that the number of water advisories is a problem that only the federal government working with our First Nations leaders can address. "Bill S-11 provides no guarantees that drinking water infrastructure will be improved in our communities. One in six of our communities is on a boil water advisory." says Robertson.
"We have support from across Canada to continue the efforts to ensure fair access to resources," Yakasovich says. "Over 600,000 students have endorsed the campaign, and we will take that support to the next level as we force the decision-makers to be accountable, and ensure our message is heard. This was an issue that was raised when Liberal Party leader Michael Ignatieff was here for a town hall meeting. We need Ottawa to understand that leaving communities behind is never an option. The electorate will not have it."
Algoma University students and people from across the country are encouraged to collect empty glasses to send to the Prime Minister's office to send the message, and promote all communities to send an empty glass with a message to the Prime Minister, asking for fair access to a safe, clean drinking water.
Contact: Katie Yakasovich, 705/949-2301 x4731, kyakasov@algomau.ca

New Jersey American Water Urges Customers to 'Follow Us' on Twitter
PR Newswire
June 17, 2010 Thursday 12:32 PM EST


Copyright 2010 PR Newswire Association LLC All Rights Reserved
Length: 356 words
Dateline: CHERRY HILL, N.J., June 17
Body


CHERRY HILL, N.J., June 17 /PRNewswire/ -- New Jersey American Water is now "tweeting" company news and updates for customers and others at Twitter.com/njamwater. The company's entry into Twitter recognizes the growing number of customers preferring social media for communicating.
New Jersey American Water is tapping Twitter to provide information about customer programs, community initiatives, environmental projects and special events, as well as alerts and updates on water emergencies, boil water advisories and water and wastewater construction projects.
"Twitter is a powerful, real-time communications tool that will help us keep customers and other interested parties up-to-date on company news and activities," said New Jersey American Water President John Bigelow. "We are excited about the ability to enhance our customer and community relations by connecting directly with everyone who follows us on Twitter."
Twitter is a free online social networking service that individuals and organizations around the world are using to communicate to others who subscribe to their updates. These updates, called "tweets," are limited to no more than 140 characters. Because of the space limitations, New Jersey American Water customers who follow the company on Twitter will be linked to the company's Web site at www.newjerseyamwater.com, as well as other online sites such as Flickr and YouTube for detailed information, photos and video.
New Jersey American Water, a wholly owned subsidiary of American Water (NYSE: AWK), is the largest investor-owned water utility in the state, providing high-quality and reliable water and/or wastewater services to approximately 2.5 million people. Founded in 1886, American Water is the largest investor-owned U.S. water and wastewater utility company. With headquarters in Voorhees, N.J., the company employs more than 7,000 dedicated professionals who provide drinking water, wastewater and other related services to approximately 16 million people in 35 states, as well as Ontario and Manitoba, Canada. More information can be found by visiting www.amwater.com.

The boil-water advisory for Green Tank Irrigation District 11 is over. Residents can now safely use their tap water without first boiling it.
The advisory was issued June 9 after water samples confirmed bacterial contamination in the water. About 170 homes and businesses served by Green Tank were affected. The district serves an area generally north of College Place and west of Walla Walla.
The state Department of Health inspected the water system and found no obvious sources of contamination. The water system has been disinfected and flushed. Lab tests show the water now meets safe drinking water standards.
No reports of illness have been associated with the advisory.

All MSDH Offices in Jackson to Return to Regular Hours on Friday, June 25
Targeted News Service
June 24, 2010 Thursday 9:49 PM EST


Copyright 2010 Targeted News Service LLC All Rights Reserved
Length: 299 words
Byline: Targeted News Service
Dateline: JACKSON, Miss.
Body


The Mississippi Department of Health issued the following news release:
The Mississippi State Department of Health (MSDH) announces that all MSDH facilities, including Hinds County Health Department clinic locations in the City of Jackson, will return to normal operations on Friday. All MSDH employees are expected to return to work at their regularly scheduled time.
The MSDH reminds those affected by City of Jackson boil water alert that as water pressure returns, water is NOT safe to drink until the boil water advisory is lifted. MSDH is working with the City of Jackson to ensure public health standards are maintained. Two consecutive days of clear water test samples must be obtained before a boil water advisory can be lifted.
Until the boil water advisory is lifted, affected residents should follow these guidelines:
* Do not drink tap water.
* Do not use ice made from recent tap water.
* Do not use tap water to make drinks, juices, or fountain soft drinks.
* Cook with tap water only if food is boiled for at least one minute.
* Wash dishes, fruits and vegetables in boiled water or water that has been disinfected with bleach.
* Brush your teeth with boiled or bottled water.
* Wash your hands and bathe as usual. Bathing is safe as long as no water is swallowed.
Take the following steps to treat water:
* Bring water to a rolling boil for 1 minute to kill most organisms.
* If you cannot boil your water, mix eight drops (1/8 teaspoon) of unscented, ordinary household chlorine bleach per gallon of water. Mix the solution thoroughly, and let stand for about 30 minutes before using.
For more information, visit the MSDH website at www.HealthyMS.com/jacksonwater or call us toll-free at 1-866-HLTHY4U (1-866-458-4948).

Two consecutive days of laboratory tests confirm that the water for customers living in the northern sections of Columbia is safe to drink. Columbia Water and Light had issued the precautionary boil advisory after a large water distribution main broke on Tuesday, June 22. The areas that were under a precautionary boil advisory were: Lake of the Woods, Mexico Gravel Road, Pine Grove Mobile Home Park, Godas, The Links, Hanover, Timber Ridge, Garden City, Indian Hills and the surrounding subdivisions.

REGION
Union ratifies contract with Giant Eagle
Local 23 of the United Food and Commercial Workers union has ratified a four-year contract with Giant Eagle.
The agreement, ratified by the union Friday by a margin of 5 to 1, covers about 5,800 workers in Allegheny, Washington and Westmoreland counties and Monongalia County in West Virginia.
It includes pay increases and improved health care benefits, according to the company.
Jim D'Alessandro, a Giant Eagle meat cutter and bargaining team member, said he was pleased with the agreement.
"Wage increases will up the standard of living for our members, the improvements to the health plan mean members will be able to take their kids to the doctors when they need to go, and we have secured the pension so they don't have to worry about living in abject poverty after a lifetime of work," he stated.
Daniel Shapira, special counsel for Giant Eagle, said, "The agreement provides attractive enhancements in wages and health care benefits, which is particularly remarkable in the current economic climate."
NORTH
Water main repairs wrap up in Aspinwall
Work on Aspinwall's big water main break has been completed.
The Pittsburgh Water and Sewer Authority reported Saturday that workers had repaired the break in a 60-inch water main that flooded parts of Freeport Road and left the area without water beginning at mid-afternoon on Tuesday.
PWSA spokeswoman Melissa Rubin said the leak was repaired by 10 Saturday morning.
Nevertheless, a boil-water advisory remains in effect for the Waterworks Mall and its customers. Ms. Rubin said a second round of tests needs to be done on water there before it can be declared safe for cooking and drinking.
The boil-water advisory for Aspinwall has been lifted by borough officials, meaning townsfolk can resume regular water use, she said.

START OF DOCUMENT







Penn Taps Manheim For Water; Flushing, Portable Filter Units Planned
Intelligencer Journal/New Era (Lancaster, Pennsylvania)
June 29, 2010 Tuesday


Copyright 2010 Lancaster Newspapers, Inc.
Section: B; Pg. 1
Length: 597 words
Byline: Civia Katz, Correspondent
Dateline: Lancaster, PA
Body


BY CIVIA KATZ
Correspondent
About 100 residents attended Penn Township supervisors meeting Monday night at Manheim Central Middle School after the township's water supply tested positive for the parasite cryptosporidium.
David Sarley, supervisor chairman, told them, "There's not going to be a magic wand waved tonight. We have to clear out the water in Penn Township and then (undergo) testing by the (state) Department of Environmental Protection. There will be a fix but not a quick fix."
The township issued a boil-water advisory on Friday. On Monday, Penn began installation of an emergency connection to the public water supply of Manheim Borough. The work is expected to be completed today.
"The whole system is already infected. As soon as you open the (water) tower, you're going to infect your entire system," Don Gibble, a resident, said.
"We're going to do the best that we can to flush the system," said Mike Wolgemuth, an employee of Severn Trent. The firm monitors the township's water and wastewater operations. "That's why the DEP will require us to keep the boil-water advisory for several days."
The township will drain the 500,000-gallon water tank and flush the lines through the fire hydrants, then refill the tank and system with water from the borough.
"Once you have flushed out the main system, what do you have to do to our homes?" resident Linda Landis asked.
After the water tank is refilled, township engineer Dan Becker said, residents will have to run their faucets and flush their toilets, but he could not give specific guidelines.
Officials said the township's bimonthly tests for cryptosporidium since November 2009 were all negative. What prompted the testing beginning June 14 was an increase in the cloudiness or turbidity of the water, which can decrease chlorine effectiveness. Tests were done daily, and the water was tested for turbidity, chlorine levels and bacteria. No bacteria, including E. coli, were found.
Dave Kratzer, township manager, said, "We are as perplexed as you are. We have been doing regular cryptosporidium testing. It was something that happened that caused this issue."
Kratzer said before the meeting that the township was looking at the formation of two sinkholes on the Kreider farm in Manheim as the potential source of the cryptosporidium contamination.
The township's only well is along Doe Run Road and adjacent to the Kreider farm.
Cryptosporidium comes from bovine feces and is found in surface water. When the sinkholes formed, the surface water possibly came into contact with the ground water that supplies the well.
Cryptosporidium is unaffected by chlorine and can only be removed by filtration or destroyed by high temperatures. It causes intestinal symptoms and can be dangerous for people who have a weak immune system.
Manheim Borough's water is filtered as well as treated with chlorine.
Kratzer said the township has completed a feasibility study required by DEP for a permanent, $2 million filtration system that is expected to be operational in 2011, two years ahead of DEP's requirement.
Penn Township has had issues with high nitrate readings that prompted the DEP to require the township to put a filtration system in place.
Kratzer said the township will bring in a portable filtration system and operate it until the permanent filtration system is completed. He said residents will no longer be exposed to unfiltered public water.
"The issues are not issues created by our fault to treat or any operator error. They are not caused by anyone's error," Kratzer said. "We've been doing this successfully for 12 years."

Load-Date: June 29, 2010
END OF DOCUMENT

VADER WATER SYSTEM CUSTOMERS ADVISED TO BOIL WATER
States News Service
July 3, 2010 Saturday


Copyright 2010 States News Service
Length: 223 words
Byline: States News Service
Dateline: OLYMPIA, WA
Body


The following information was released by the Washington State Department of Health:
The state Department of Health is advising customers of the Vader water system in Lewis County to boil their drinking water until further notice. The health advisory is being issued because of a break in one of the city's distribution lines that occurred late last night.
The break caused an outage to about five homes on the system. Service to those homes has been restored. It also caused the entire system to lose pressure, which could allow bacteria and other contaminants to enter the water system. The advisory affects about 600 residents.
The city is working to restore service, disinfect, and flush the system and test water for contaminants. The boil water advisory is likely to last through the holiday weekend until water quality tests show the water is safe to drink.
State health officials advise customers to use boiled or purchased bottled water for drinking, brushing teeth, dishwashing, preparing food, and making ice. Tap water should be boiled for one minute and allowed to cool before use.
Vader has been dealing with aging system problems that have caused multiple outages and the need to issue health advisories in the past few years. The department is working with Vader and Lewis County on a long-term solution to their water problems.

The city is working to restore service, disinfect, and flush the system and test water for contaminants. The boil water advisory is likely to last through the holiday weekend until water quality tests show the water is safe to drink.
State health officials advise customers to use boiled or purchased bottled water for drinking, brushing teeth, dishwashing, preparing food, and making ice. Tap water should be boiled for one minute and allowed to cool before use.
Vader has been dealing with aging system problems that have caused multiple outages and the need to issue health advisories in the past few years. The department is working with Vader and Lewis County on a long-term solution to their water problems.

Judith, Narragansett North End, South Kingstown South Shore, and South Kingstown Middlebridge water systems. HEALTH recommends that water being used for drinking, making ice, brushing teeth, cooking or bathing of infants should be boiled for one minute and allowed to cool before using. United Water and the towns of Narragansett and South Kingstown have banned all outdoor water use until further notice. In addition, the Department of Environmental Management (DEM) has agreed to close cold-water showers at state beaches.
This boil water advisory is in effect until further notice from HEALTH. Customers of United Water, Narragansett Pt. Judith, and Narragansett North End, South Kingstown South Shore, and South Kingstown Middlebridge water systems are asked to contact neighbors who may not be aware of this advisory. Byline: States News Service
Dateline: OLYMPIA, WA
Body


The following information was released by the Washington State Department of Health:
Customers of the City of Vader water system no longer have to boil their drinking water. A health advisory issued Saturday has ended because lab tests received today show the water meets safe drinking water standards.
The utility issued the advisory after a water main broke, causing an outage to about five homes and loss of pressure throughout the water distribution system. The pressure loss could have allowed contaminated or untreated water to be drawn into the system, so the advisory was issued as a public health precaution. About 600 residents in the Lewis County community were affected.
Utility crews repaired the broken water main, flushed the lines, verified chlorine levels in the system and took numerous water samples to test for bacterial contamination.
City, county, and state officials will hold a public meeting on July 20 to discuss the future of Vader's water system. The meeting will be from 6:30 to 8 p.m. at Vader's Lions Hall.
Vader has been dealing with aging water system problems for the past several years. The state Department of Health is working with the city and Lewis County on a long-term solution.
Customers who have questions about their water may call 360-295-3222.

Copyright 2010 Targeted News Service LLC All Rights Reserved
Length: 197 words
Byline: Targeted News Service
Dateline: COLUMBIA, Mo.
Body


The city of Columbia issued the following news release:
A 12-inch water main on Blackfoot Road broke late this afternoon which caused the pressure to drop substantially. According to standards set by the Department of Natural Resources, Columbia Water & Light issued a precautionary water boil advisory.
Customers living on Blackfoot Road, Cedar Cliff Drive and Kraemer Court are urged to take the following precautions:
* Boil water for three minutes prior to using it for cooking or drinking.
* Do not use ice from an automatic ice maker. Remake ice with water that has been boiled.
* Disinfect dishes and food contact surfaces by immersing for one minute in clean tap water that contains one teaspoon of unscented bleach per gallon of water.
Crews are working on restoring water service to the area. Columbia Water & Light must have two clean samples before lifting the water boil advisory which will take a minimum of 48 hours for processing. Customers will be notified with hang tags on their doors that the boil advisory has been lifted.

BOIL WATER ADVISORY ISSUED AT BLUFFVIEW IN SAUK COUNTY
States News Service
July 12, 2010 Monday


Copyright 2010 States News Service
Length: 261 words
Byline: States News Service
Dateline: MADISON, WI
Body


The following information was released by the Wisconsin Department of Natural Resources:
A boil water advisory has been issued for residents of Bluffview, located along U.S. 12 in Sauk County about seven miles south of Baraboo, the state Department of Natural Resources reported Thursday afternoon.
All residents on the west side of Highway 12 are advised to boil their water prior to drinking or preparing food. Ice, food and any beverages prepared with unsafe water must be discarded. Persons in Bluffview should boil or use commercially bottled water for drinking, food preparation and making ice. If you boil water, the water should be heated to a rolling boil for at least one minute before use. Ice should be made from boiled or bottled water.
A water sample collected July 1 indicated the presence of coliform bacteria. Further sampling July 6 confirmed their presence. While coliform bacteria, naturally present in the environment, are not generally harmful themselves, they are an indicator that other, potentially-harmful, bacteria may be present.
Coliforms were found in more samples than allowed and this was a warning of potential problems. Whenever the DNR detects coliform bacteria in any sample, the department does follow-up testing to see if other bacteria of greater concern, such as fecal coliform or E. coli, are present. The department did not find any of these bacteria in subsequent testing.
The advisory will be lifted when there are two rounds of safe samples, said Dave Barkhahn, DNR water supply engineer. A notice will be issued when that occurs.

Load-Date: July 13, 2010
END OF DOCUMENT

START OF DOCUMENT







Penn Lifts Boil-Water Advisory
Intelligencer Journal/New Era (Lancaster, Pennsylvania)
July 14, 2010 Wednesday


Copyright 2010 Lancaster Newspapers, Inc.
Section: B; Pg. 5
Length: 475 words
Byline: Civia Katz, Correspondent
Dateline: Lancaster, PA
Body


BY CIVIA KATZ
Correspondent
Penn Township removed the boil-water advisory Tuesday, nearly three weeks after the public water supply tested positive for the parasite cryptosporidium.
Notices were hand-delivered to residents.
Cryptosporidium, a bacterium, was detected in the water on June 25. The state Department of Environmental Protection approved a plan for the township to flush out the system.
Dave Kratzer, township manager, said Monday the last two tests conducted by the township for the parasite came back negative.
The township had to wait 18-hours after running the normal bacteria test for E. coli and chloroforms on Monday before the DEP gave the all clear.
The township installed a portable filtering system at a cost of $25,000 per month to filter all township water. The system provides a 0.1 micron filtering system. The size of the cryptosporidium is 3 to 5 microns. Cryptosporidium bacteria are resistant to chlorine but can be filtered out or killed with high temperatures.
"There has not been untreated water entering the system since July 2," Kratzer said Monday.
The portable filtering system will remain in place until the permanent water filtration system is built and online, which is expected to next year. The project is expected to cost about $3 million.
After the bacteria alert, the township shut down its well and tapped into Manheim Borough's water supply to try to provide filtered water for the residents. Manheim Borough could not provide the amount of water needed because of poor infrastructure, Dave Sarley, Penn supervisor chairman, said Monday.
The borough has an aging system of pipes, and maps of the system are incomplete. Sarley said the borough has the water capacity, but not the facilities to support it.
The borough "had paved over a valve that was closed. They did not even know they had it. (Township Supervisor Daryl) Lefever found it and dug it up," said Sarley. "Five minutes after we hooked into borough water, people were out of water. There may be a lot of water there, but it could not get here."
The township had to put the well back online to supplement the water from the borough, Sarley said, and the township disconnected from the borough water system Monday.
He said the township has no plans to permanently connect to the borough water supply in the future.
The township provided residents with guidelines from the Centers for Disease Control and Prevention when the boil-water advisory was lifted. The guidelines advise residents to flush pipes and faucets.
Guidelines include running cold-water faucets continuously for five minutes, making and discarding three batches of ice from automatic ice makers, running water softeners through a regeneration cycle, draining and refilling water heaters set below 113 degrees Fahrenheit and changing filters on all point-of-entry and point-of-use water filters.

Load-Date: July 15, 2010
END OF DOCUMENT

NMED Lifts 'Boil Water Advisory' for Kamp Kiwanis in McKinley County
Targeted News Service
July 14, 2010 Wednesday 2:24 AM EST


Copyright 2010 Targeted News Service LLC All Rights Reserved
Length: 327 words
Byline: Targeted News Service
Dateline: SANTA FE, N.M.
Body


The New Mexico Department of the Environment issued the following news release:
The New Mexico Environment Department's (NMED) Drinking Water Bureau advised the Kamp Kiwanis to lift a "boil water advisory" for its water system.
NMED issued the advisory after bacteriological contamination that exceeded the Maximum Contaminant Level for E. coli was discovered in drinking water from the water system. NMED required the Kamp Kiwanis non-community water system in McKinley County to notify its consumers of the finding.
Actions to disinfect the water system and identify possible sources of contamination were promptly taken. These actions included shock chlorination. Consumers were advised to boil all water prior to ingestion.
Water samples collected on July 10 and July 12, 2010 have shown no E. coli present in the water system. These clean results have allowed NMED's Drinking Water Bureau to advise Kamp Kiwanis to lift the "boil water advisory" for its water system.
The presence of E. coli in water indicates that the water may have been in contact with sewage or animal wastes, and could contain disease-causing organisms. Most strains of E. coli are harmless and live in the intestines of healthy humans and animals. However, a positive test for E. coli in the drinking water supply may indicate the presence of dangerous strains of E. coli or other disease-causing organisms, which are sometimes found in sewage or animal wastes. These types of organisms may cause severe gastrointestinal illness and, in rare cases, even death. Children, the elderly and immuno-compromised individuals are at an increased risk for illness.
For more information, call NMED Communications Director Marissa Stone Bardino at (505) 827-0314 or (505) 231-0475 or the DWB Water System Specialist Diane Barnes at 505-566-9744.
Contact: Marissa Stone Bardino, Communications Director, 505/827-0314, 505/231-0475

BOIL WATER ADVISORY ISSUED FOR THE CITY OF MINNEAPOLIS
States News Service
July 15, 2010 Thursday


Copyright 2010 States News Service
Length: 314 words
Byline: States News Service
Dateline: TOPEKA, KS
Body


The following information was released by the Kansas Department of Health and Environment:
The Kansas Department of Health and Environment (KDHE) has issued a boil water advisory for the City of Minneapolis, which is located in Ottawa County.
KDHE officials are issuing the advisory due to a break in a water main, which resulted in a loss of pressure in the distribution system. The water main is in the process of being repaired and whenever such a loss of pressure occurs, it is possible for contaminants to enter the system. Also during this time, disinfection (chlorine) residuals may drop to levels that are inadequate to protect against bacterial contamination.
Residents in the City of Minneapolis served by the affected public water system should observe the following precautions:
Boil water vigorously for one minute prior to use. Boiling longer than three minutes may adversely affect the quality and taste of the water.
Use only boiled water for drinking, brushing teeth, diluting fruit juices, and all other food preparation.
Dispose of ice cubes and do not use ice from a household automatic icemaker. Remake ice cubes with water that has been boiled.
Disinfect dishes and other food contact surfaces by immersion for at least one minute in clean tap water that contains one teaspoon of unscented household bleach per gallon of water.
Water used for bathing does not generally need to be boiled. Supervision of children is necessary while bathing or using backyard pools so water is not ingested. Persons with cuts or severe rashes may wish to consult their physicians.
The advisory will remain in effect until testing of water samples indicates no evidence of contamination and all other conditions which place the systems at risk of contamination are deemed by KDHE officials to be resolved. The city and/or KDHE will notify media when the boil water advisory has been rescinded.

START OF DOCUMENT







Gov. Beshear Meets with Pike County Officials Following Flooding
Targeted News Service
July 19, 2010 Monday 10:14 PM EST


Copyright 2010 Targeted News Service LLC All Rights Reserved
Length: 620 words
Byline: Targeted News Service
Dateline: FRANKFORT, Ky.
Body


Gov. Steve Beshear, D-Ky., issued the following news release:
Governor Steve Beshear visited areas of Pike County today following weekend storms that caused severe flooding and mudslides. The storms are blamed for two deaths in Pike County.
"I have seen startling and significant damage in Pike County today," said Gov. Beshear. "My administration, from Emergency Management to the Transportation Cabinet and beyond, is working quickly to get these struggling Kentucky families the help they need."
Gov. Beshear's trip included stops at Raccoon Creek and a meeting with local officials at the Pike County Courthouse. Gov. Beshear declared a State of Emergency on Sunday for Pike and Shelby counties and requested Federal Emergency Management Agency (FEMA) to conduct preliminary damage assessments. Seven FEMA assessment teams will begin work tomorrow.
"My heart goes out to the hundreds of families impacted by this torrential flooding. I want to assure the people of Pike County that help is on the way and we will utilize every resource to help those paralyzed by this natural disaster," said Congressman Hal Rogers. "I applaud the Governor for declaring a state of emergency and as necessary, I will be working with officials here in Washington to make sure that things are moving as quickly as possible to bring temporary relief while we begin the rebuilding process. While more challenges lie ahead, I know the resilient people of Pike County and together we will overcome this tragedy and become a stronger community."
Up to eight inches of rain fell in a short period of time, prompting emergency evacuations and rescues. Pike Co. Emergency Management officials estimate approximately 200 homes were damaged or destroyed by the weekend's flooding and mudslides.
"It looks more like a tornado has been through here than a flood in some places," said Pike County Judge Executive Wayne T. Rutherford. "This is the most devastating flood I have ever seen. But we are resilient in these mountains and we will pull through it."
Approximately 400 residents remain without power in Pike County, down from more than 7,000 Sunday. Approximately 13,500 residents are without water, and another 13,000 are under a boil water advisory. Water distribution points will operate until restoration is complete. One shelter remains open at Pike Central High School, where 25 people stayed Sunday night. The Kentucky Community Crises Response Board (KCCRB) sent a counseling team to the area on Sunday and is expected to have expanded teams in the county beginning today.
Safety Tips
* Kentuckians are encouraged to monitor river and streams crests for their areas and heed warnings or evacuation orders from local officials. Do not drive through or wade through any water, no matter if just a few inches. STOP, TURN AROUND - DON'T DROWN!
* Do not attempt to enter flooded structures unless a certified electrician has shut the power off.
* Be aware of toxic or hazardous wastes associated with flood waters. For additional information on health safety tips and flood water clean-up, please visit the Department for Public Health's website at www.chfs.ky.gov/dph/.
* For statewide road conditions please visit www.511.ky.gov .
* For local information and or shelter locations, please contact your local emergency management office. Follow this link for assistance: http://www.kyem.ky.gov/about/countyemdirectors.htm .
* For river levels and expected crests, visit http://water.weather.gov/ahps/ and click on the area you wish to observe.
* For additional information on this and other Kentucky disasters, please visit www.kyem.ky.gov .
Contact: Kerri Richardson, 502/564-2611
Copyright Targeted News Services
TNS C-BhaS 100720-mv45-2920226 61MarlynVitin

Load-Date: July 20, 2010
END OF DOCUMENT

START OF DOCUMENT







Damage Assessment Teams Begin Work in Pike County
Targeted News Service
July 20, 2010 Tuesday 3:29 AM EST


Copyright 2010 Targeted News Service LLC All Rights Reserved
Length: 629 words
Byline: Targeted News Service
Dateline: FRANKFORT, Ky.
Body


Gov. Steve Beshear, D-Ky., issued the following news release:
Through a coordinated joint effort, Preliminary Damage Assessment (PDA) teams consisting of personnel from local, state and federal government have begun gathering damage estimates from local government and private citizens in Pike County.
"The aftermath of the flooding in Pike County is really unlike anything I've seen before," said Gov. Beshear, who visited the area yesterday to meet with local officials. "Swiftly moving water is extremely dangerous and its ability to cause destruction should never be underestimated."
Federal Emergency Management Agency (FEMA) personnel arrived in Pike County yesterday. After being briefed by local and Kentucky Division of Emergency Management (KYEM) officials, teams were assembled and county assessments were assigned. These teams will begin PDAs throughout the county today. These damage assessments will be used to support Gov. Beshear's request for federal assistance.
"We are hoping to expedite the assistance process by having the FEMA teams conduct these damage assessments with our local teams," said John Heltzel, director for KYEM. "We want to bring whatever assistance is needed, and eligible, to all of Pike County and its residents as soon as possible."
Officials encourage those who have suffered property damage to photograph the damage, save any repair receipts and report your damage to the local emergency management director.
The Kentucky National Guard currently has 24 Soldiers on duty providing support to Pike County. For the past several days, members of the 577th Sapper Company, 201st Engineer Battalion have conducted security patrols in humvees in support of local law enforcement, and UH-60 Black Hawk helicopter crews have assisted in damage assessment. Additional troops from the 201st are being brought on to provide communications and logistical support in the distribution of bottled water.
If you do not have the family and/or financial resources to clean out your property, you can call 606-432-0210 to request volunteer assistance. "Folks need to be aware volunteer groups are available to help clean up they cannot dismantle or remove destroyed homes," said Jim Garrett, Voluntary Agency Liaison for Volunteer Organizations Active in Disaster (VOAD).
Safety Messages:
* Do not drive through or wade through any water, no matter if it's just a few inches. STOP - TURN AROUND - DON'T DROWN!
* The Kentucky Division of Water (DOW) reports that boil water advisories are in effect for much of the county due to broken lines and other factors. Water distribution points have been established to assist those without water. Check with your local government for current water distribution locations.
* DOW also warns against contact with floodwaters due to contamination from sewage, agricultural products and other harmful substances.
* The Kentucky Department of Public Health (DPH) encourages flooded residents to be aware of toxic or hazardous wastes associated with flood waters. For additional information on health safety tips and flood water clean-up, please visit the DPH's website at www.chfs.ky.gov/dph/ or contact the local health department.
* Do not attempt to enter flooded structures unless a certified electrician has shut the power off.
* Avoid unnecessary sight seeing, keeping the roadways clear and allowing emergency officials access to the impacted areas.
For local information and/or shelter locations, please contact your local emergency management office. Follow this link for assistance: http://www.kyem.ky.gov/about/countyemdirectors.htm .
For additional information, visit the KyEM website at www.kyem.ky.gov.
Contact: Kerri Richardson, 502/564-2611
Copyright Targeted News Services
TNS C-BhaS 100721-mv45-2922526 61MarlynVitin

Load-Date: July 21, 2010

START OF DOCUMENT







Penn Will Cut Water Bills
Intelligencer Journal/New Era (Lancaster, Pennsylvania)
July 21, 2010 Wednesday


Copyright 2010 Lancaster Newspapers, Inc.
Section: B; Pg. 7
Length: 311 words
Byline: Civia Katz, Correspondent
Dateline: Lancaster, PA
Body


BY CIVIA KATZ
Correspondent
Penn Township is rebating water costs to residents placed under a boil water advisory for nearly three weeks that ended July 13.
About 575 water customers will receive a 25 percent discount on their water bills.
"We will prorate your water bills for the 22 days. We will adjust the bills so your water bills will be discounted," Dave Sarley, supervisor chairman, said July 12.
The township issued a boil water advisory when a parasite, cryptosporidium, was found in the water supply. At the time, the township water was not filtered. It was treated with chlorine, which cryptosporidium is resistant to.
Cryptosporidium causes intestinal symptoms, especially in people who have a suppressed immune system.
Township Manager Dave Kratzer said July 12 that the township had received no reports of illness.
The township brought in a portable system July 2 at a cost of $25,000 a month. The rented unit will filter the water until a permanent system is built sometime in 2011. Kratzer said the township will not be passing on these costs to the residents.
Public water users were without water for a period of 45 minutes during the boil water advisory. In an e-mail dated July 16, Kratzer said the outage occurred July 11 and was caused by an electrical issue with a motor.
The interconnection that the township tried with the Manheim Borough Water Authority did not provide adequate pressure to supply water to higher elevations of the water system. As a result, Kratzer said, the water storage tank went offline.
The future filtration plant will cost the township about $3 million. It will filter out bacteria and also address the nitrate issues the township has had with the public water.
The township had two high nitrate readings in February, which triggered the need for a feasibility study required by the state Department of Environmental Protection.

Load-Date: July 21, 2010
