START OF DOCUMENT







GOV. BESHEAR DECLARES STATE OF EMERGENCY FOLLOWING STORMS AND FLOODING
States News Service
July 21, 2010 Wednesday


Copyright 2010 States News Service
Length: 710 words
Byline: States News Service
Dateline: FRANKFORT, KY
Body


The following information was released by the office of the governor of Kentucky:
Governor Steve Beshear today declared a State of Emergency in Kentucky following severe storms that struck Pike and Shelby counties early Sunday morning and several northeastern Kentuckian counties late Tuesday night and early Wednesday morning. The storms have caused flash flooding, evacuations and water rescues in the northeastern Kentucky counties of Carter, Elliott, Lewis, Mason and Rowan counties. Those counties have each declared states of emergency; the cities of Olive Hill and Maysville have also declared local states of emergency.
Gov. Beshear also signed an executive order today to trigger the price gouging statutes that protect consumers from unscrupulous businesses that attempt to artificially inflate prices as a result of the emergency.
The executive order will allow for investigation into any complaints of price gouging that may occur relative to gas, heating, building supplies, hotels and other goods and services in the aftermath of the weekend's storms.
Weather reports indicate as much as six inches of rain has fallen on parts of northeast Kentucky. The Little Sandy River is rising and expected to crest above flood stage in Grayson. American Electric Power reports approximately 566 customers in Letcher, Carter and Lewis counties are currently without power. Approximately 400 Lewis County homes are currently without water.
In Carter County, a shelter operated by the Salvation Army has opened at Grahn Community Center. Early estimates indicate that 50 to 60 homes in Carter County were affected by the floods, approximately 20 of which are destroyed. Eight roads are currently underwater in Fleming County. KY-57 is closed at the Fleming-Lewis county line and multiple roads are closed in the Laurel Camp Dix area in Lewis County. Forty homes in Rowan County have been flooded, two of which have been destroyed. At least 100 cars were flooded, and 20 county bridges and 20 private bridges with approaches have been washed out.
Officials expect the amount of damages to increase as water recedes in the impacted counties, as emergency workers and local officials will be able to reach areas previously under water and hope to have a better assessment on the extent of damage.
These latest floods came just days after heavy thunderstorms hit Pike and Shelby counties. Two fatalities are attributed to the Pike County storms. Gov. Steve Beshear declared states of emergency for both counties over the weekend. Federal Emergency Management Agency (FEMA) assessment teams have been working to evaluate damages in Pike County for two days, which will expedite the process for applying for any applicable federal assistance.
Pike County updates
Local, state and federal damage assessment teams continue assessing the property damage in Pike County.
In Pike County, 2,400 residents remain without water and much of the county remains on boil water advisories. Volunteers are taking drinking water to impacted areas, and water distribution points have been established throughout the county. Three shelters are open in the area.
Safety Tips
Kentuckians are encouraged to monitor weather (www.weather.com) for their areas and heed warnings or evacuation orders from local officials. Do not drive through or wade through any water, no matter if just a few inches. STOP, TURN AROUND DON'T DROWN!
Do not attempt to enter flooded structures unless a certified electrician has shut off the power.
For additional information and safety tips, please visit KyEM's website at www.kyem.ky.gov.
Be aware of toxic or hazardous wastes associated with flood waters. For additional information on health safety tips and flood water clean-up, please visit the Department for Public Health's website at www.chfs.ky.gov/dph/.
For statewide road conditions please visit www.511.ky.gov .
For local information and or shelter locations, please contact your local emergency management office. Follow this link for assistance: http://www.kyem.ky.gov/about/countyemdirectors.htm .
For river levels and expected crests, visit http://water.weather.gov/ahps/ and click on the area you wish to observe.
For additional information on this and other Kentucky disasters, please visit www.kyem.ky.gov .

Load-Date: July 22, 2010
END OF DOCUMENT

Environment Department Issues 'Boil Water Advisory' for El Vadito de Los Cerrillos Water Association Water System
Targeted News Service
July 23, 2010 Friday 2:13 AM EST


Copyright 2010 Targeted News Service LLC All Rights Reserved
Length: 382 words
Byline: Targeted News Service
Dateline: SANTA FE, N.M.
Body


The New Mexico Department of the Environment issued the following news release:
The New Mexico Environment Department's Drinking Water Bureau has issued a "boil water advisory" for the El Vadito de Los Cerrillos Water Association Water System.
NMED issued the advisory on July 23, 2010 after bacteriological contamination that exceeded the Maximum Contaminant Level for E. coli was discovered in drinking water at the water system. NMED requires the El Vadito de Los Cerrillos Water Association to notify water consumers of the finding. The El Vadito de Los Cerrillos Water Association Water System is located approximately 20 miles south of Santa Fe. This advisory only applies to customers served by the El Vadito de Los Cerrillos Water Association, and does not extend to any of the other surrounding water systems or communities.
Consumers of water at the El Vadito de Los Cerrillos Water Association Water System are advised to boil the water for five minutes before drinking, cooking, dishwashing and bathing. The presence of E. coli in water indicates that the water may have been in contact with sewage or animal wastes, and could contain disease-causing organisms. Most strains of E. coli are harmless and live in the intestines of healthy humans and animals. However, a positive test for E. coli in the drinking water supply may indicate the presence of dangerous strains of E. coli or other disease-causing organisms. These types of organisms may cause severe gastrointestinal illness and, in rare cases, death. Children, the elderly and immuno-compromised individuals are at an increased risk for illness.
Actions have been initiated to disinfect the water system and identify possible sources of contamination, establish acceptable disinfection, and flush out the water system. The NMED Drinking Water Bureau will provide technical assistance to the water system and will test the water until no further threat of contamination remains.
For more information, call NMED Communications Director Marissa Stone Bardino at (505) 827-0314 or (505) 231-0475 or Mike Huber, Drinking Water Bureau Compliance Manager, at (505) 660-3834.
Contact: Marissa Stone Bardino, NMED Communications Director, 505/827-0314, 505/231-0475
Copyright Targeted News Services
TNS hc11-JF78100726-2928208 StaffFurigay

Boil Water Advisory Lifted for Campus and Area
Targeted News Service
July 25, 2010 Sunday 6:01 AM EST


Copyright 2010 Targeted News Service LLC All Rights Reserved
Length: 110 words
Byline: Targeted News Service
Dateline: WILMINGTON, N.C.
Body


The University of North Carolina-Wilmington issued the following news release:
According to the Cape Fear Public Utility Authority (CFPUA), the Boil Water Advisory implemented on Friday has been lifted and mandatory water conservation measures are no longer in effect for UNCW and other CFPUA customers. The original advisory was the result of a major water main break on Friday, July 23, on Cornelius Harnett Drive. Water analysis is now complete and the water distribution system is now functioning under normal operations.
For additional details, refer to the CFPUA website at www.cfpua.org/.

Damage Assessments Continuing in Hard Hit Counties
Targeted News Service
July 26, 2010 Monday 11:59 PM EST


Copyright 2010 Targeted News Service LLC All Rights Reserved
Length: 604 words
Byline: Targeted News Service
Dateline: FRANKFORT, Ky.
Body


Gov. Steve Beshear, D-Ky., issued the following news release:
Gov. Steve Beshear today said that local emergency management officials continue conducting damage assessments from last week's devastating storms, which caused severe flooding in several northeastern Kentucky counties.
Gov. Beshear was notified late Friday afternoon that President Barack Obama approved his request for a major disaster declaration for Pike County for assistance from the severe storms and flooding that hit Saturday, July 17, causing two fatalities and severe damage across the county. This presidential declaration came just two days after the Governor made his request to the president for federal assistance.
"I am extremely pleased that we were able to validate the damage, submit the request and be awarded federal assistance so quickly," said Gov. Beshear. "I am also pleased that as soon as other counties hit the eligibility thresholds we will be able to add them to the existing presidential major disaster declaration. Not having to submit separate requests for each impacted county will greatly expedite the delivery of necessary federal assistance."
Shelby County was also hard hit by storms on July 17, and damage assessments are underway. Carter, Elliot, Lawrence, Lewis, Mason and Rowan counties declared state of emergencies due to severe flooding on July 20 and 21 and damage assessments are continuing in those counties. If those counties reach the required damage threshold, they will be added to the President's major disaster declaration. Approximately 2,225 customers remain on boiled water advisories in these northeastern Kentucky counties.
Details of the Pike County Disaster Declaration, KY-1925
July 23 - President Obama granted federal disaster assistance for both Individual Assistance (IA) and Public Assistance (PA) for Pike County:
* The President's action makes federal funding available to affected individuals in Pike County.
* Assistance can include grants for temporary housing and home repairs, low-cost loans to cover uninsured property losses and other programs to help individuals and business owners recover from the effects of the disaster.
* Federal funding also is available to the state and eligible local governments and certain private nonprofit organizations on a cost-sharing basis for emergency work and the repair or replacement of facilities damaged by the severe storms, flooding and mudslides in Pike County.
* Federal funding is also available on a cost-sharing basis for hazard mitigation measures statewide.
* Pike County residents and business owners who sustained losses can begin applying for assistance by registering online at www.DisasterAssistance.gov or by calling 1-800-621-FEMA (3362) or 1-800-462-7585 (TTY) for the hearing and speech impaired. The toll-free telephone numbers will operate from 7 a.m. to 10 p.m. (local time). Residents MUST register with FEMA to be eligible for assistance.
* Federal Emergency Management Agency (FEMA) Mobile Disaster Recovery Centers opened earlier today in Pike County at two locations: in the lower parking lot of Pikeville/Pike County Community Funeral Home located on Zebulon Highway and the second location is at the mouth of Harlesses' Creek on US Hwy 460 at Community Bank.
* Approximately 25,000 Pike County customers remain on boiled water advisories and 75 residents on Harlesses' Creek are without water.
For additional disaster recovery information, including FEMA assistance programs, visit the KyEM website at www.kyem.ky.gov.

Expert Joins Penn Water Authority
Intelligencer Journal/New Era (Lancaster, Pennsylvania)
August 4, 2010 Wednesday


Copyright 2010 Lancaster Newspapers, Inc.
Section: B; Pg. 6
Length: 296 words
Byline: Civia Katz, Correspondent
Dateline: Lancaster, PA
Body


BY CIVIA KATZ
Correspondent
Penn Township approved the appointment of resident Charles Smith to the Northwestern Lancaster County Authority at the July 12 supervisors meeting.
Smith, an expert on cryptosporidium, offered his services when the parasite was found in the public water system in June. "This is one of the more positive things that came out of the water crisis," Dave Sarley, supervisor chairman, said. "He's an expert on all these little bugs."
Smith is a certified water technologist. He said only 400 people hold this certification nationally, and it represents the highest credential in the industrial and commercial water treatment field. Smith was one of the first 60 people to receive the certification. Exam requirements exam include five years of experience investigating water treatment problems and implementing corrective action.
"He has impeccable credentials," Sarley said. "With his knowledge of cryptosporidium, I said I got to have this guy. We're happy to have you."
When the parasite was found in the water, the township issued a boil water advisory. Smith told supervisors and about 20 residents at the meeting the parasite is a macro organism that can be filtered out of the water system. It is a hardy parasite that is encapsulated, protecting it from chemicals like chlorine.
"Cryptosporidium has to complete its life cycle. It needs a warm host to complete its cycle," Smith said. Without a host, the cryptosporidium cannot reproduce, and it is not harmful, he said.
Mike Wolgemuth of Severn Trent, the firm that oversees the water treatment, said eight cryptosporidium were found in the water. Since July 2, the township water has used a temporary water filtration system that will be operational until a permanent filtering plant is built next year.

Environment Department Lifts 'Boil Water Advisory' for Tajique MDWCA in Torrance County
Targeted News Service
August 5, 2010 Thursday 3:33 AM EST


Copyright 2010 Targeted News Service LLC All Rights Reserved
Length: 247 words
Byline: Targeted News Service
Dateline: SANTA FE, N.M.
Body


The New Mexico Department of the Environment issued the following news release:
The New Mexico Environment Department's Drinking Water Bureau is lifting a "boil water advisory" for the Tajique Mutual Domestic Water Consumers Association on the east side of the Manzano Mountains in Torrance County.
NMED issued the advisory on April 21 due to multiple failures by the Tajique MDWCA to test for bacteria in the drinking water as required by the New Mexico Drinking Water Regulations. The association, which is a small community water system, serves approximately 180 people. NMED required the Tajique MDWCA to notify its customers and members that the water system was not meeting the water sampling and reporting requirements. While there was no indication of contamination of the drinking water, without bacteria water sample results NMED could not be certain of the safety of the water provided by the Tajique MDWCA.
Subsequent water quality samples have shown no bacteriological contamination of the water system. These clean results have allowed NMED's Drinking Water Bureau to lift the "boil water advisory" for the Tajique MDWCA.
For more information, call NMED Communications Director Marissa Stone Bardino at (505) 827-0314 or (505) 231-0475 or Mike Huber, Drinking Water Bureau Compliance Manager, at (505) 660-3834.

August 13, 2010 Friday 2:42 AM EST


Copyright 2010 Targeted News Service LLC All Rights Reserved
Length: 229 words
Byline: Targeted News Service
Dateline: SANTA FE, N.M.
Body


The New Mexico Department of the Environment issued the following news release:
The New Mexico Environment Department's Drinking Water Bureau is lifting a "boil water advisory" for the Tecolote Mutual Domestic Water Consumers Association (MDWCA)Water System.
NMED issued the advisory on August 2, 2010 after bacteriological contamination that exceeded the Maximum Contaminant Level for E. coli was discovered in the water system. NMED required the Tecolote Water System to notify all water consumers of the finding.
Corrective actions were taken by the water system, including disinfecting the water system by increasing the level of chlorination and identifying possible sources of contamination. Consumers were advised to boil all water prior to ingestion.
Water samples collected since the corrective actions were taken have shown no E. coli present in the water system. These clean results have allowed NMED's Drinking Water Bureau to advise the Tecolote MDWCA Water System to lift the "boil water advisory" for the water system.

Akron Issues Boil Water Advisory
Intelligencer Journal/New Era (Lancaster, Pennsylvania)
August 14, 2010 Saturday


Copyright 2010 Lancaster Newspapers, Inc.
Section: B; Pg. 2
Length: 209 words
Byline: Diana Martin
Dateline: Lancaster, PA
Body


Residents in Akron Borough are urged to boil water after a well tested positive for E. coli Thursday.
Bacteria was found in one of the borough's eight public wells. The well has been taken off-line and the plant is increasing chlorination and flushing out the system.
The area's 4,000 residents have been put on a boil-water advisory until further notice. The problem is anticipated to be resolved by Friday, Mayor John McBeth said.
E. coli are bacteria whose presence indicates that the water may be contaminated with human or animal wastes, the advisory stated.
Microbes in these wastes can cause diarrhea, cramps, nausea, headaches, or other symptoms. They may pose a special health risk for infants, young children, some of the elderly and people with severely compromised immune systems.
"Drink boiled or bottled," reminded McBeth.
Boiled water should also be used for making ice, brushing teeth, washing dishes and food preparation.
In July, water in Penn Township tested positive for the parasite cryptosporidium. Residents were put on a 3-week boil-water advisory.
Since July 2, the township has been using a temporary water filtration system. A permanent water filtration system will be built next year, at an estimated cost of $3 million.
dmartin@lnpnews.com

Boil Water Advisory Remains in Effect; Water Volume Restrictions to be Lifted
Targeted News Service
August 14, 2010 Saturday 9:59 PM EST


Copyright 2010 Targeted News Service LLC All Rights Reserved
Length: 428 words
Byline: Targeted News Service
Dateline: AMES, Iowa
Body


The city of Ames issued the following news release:
As flushing efforts conclude, the City of Ames' Water Department has announced that the water volume restrictions will be lifted as of 2 p.m. today, including restrictions on exterior water use. Ames citizens will be able to resume their normal water usage, including laundry, toilet flushing, showers/bathing and outdoor debris clean-up. The boil advisory will remain in effect for Ames citizens until further notice.
"We have made tremendous progress," said John Dunn, director of the City's Water and Pollution Control Department. "We are progressing better than I dared to hope, but we ask that the public please continue their conservation efforts and don't start using mass amounts of water prior to 2 p.m., as we need to allow the water towers to fill up again."
Dunn said that crews did respond to a four-inch water main break last night along Murray Drive but repairs were completed by 11 p.m.
Ames citizens are reminded that while the volume restrictions will be lifted, the water is still not safe for human consumption. Water coming from the tap should still not be used for purposes such as drinking, brushing teeth, washing dishes, preparing food, and making ice, unless boiled or treated first. Both commercial and residential dishwashers are also not considered effective means of sanitizing the water.
So far, 88 water samples have been collected by the Water and Pollution Control Department, with 90 more water samples scheduled to be collected today.
Safe drinking water will continue to be distributed at all four locations in Ames until the boil advisory is lifted. These sites include Sam's Club on Airport Road, McFarland Clinic West (next to West HyVee), ISU Towers parking lot, and Wal-Mart on Grand Avenue. Residents may pick up two gallons of water per person each day.
As of 6:00 Saturday morning, water readings for Squaw Creek and the Skunk River were:
* Squaw Creek at Lincoln Way: 4.6 feet
* Skunk River at Riverside Drive: 8.73 feet
* Skunk River at U.S. 30: 18.52 feet
"Health and safety have been, and will continue to be, our main focus," said Mayor Ann Campbell. "The community's response and cooperation is greatly appreciated."
All roads in Ames are now open but drivers are asked to use caution, as there may be debris in some locations.
A 4 p.m. press conference is scheduled for Sunday, August 15, in the council chambers, for further flood updates.
Contact: Susan Gwiasda, Public Relations Officer, 515/239-5204

The Oklahoma Department of Environmental Quality issued the following news release:
The Oklahoma Department of Environmental Quality (DEQ) has advised Shady Valley Mobile Home Park, located in Pottawatomie County, to inform consumers of the drinking water that it is unsafe for human consumption due to the presence of E. coli.
The boil advisory was issued after water samples indicated the presence of E. coli. To ensure the water is safe for human consumption, water served from the Shady Valley Mobile Home Park system should be vigorously boiled for at least one minute before drinking, use in food preparation, washing dishes or brushing teeth.
The advisory to boil water will remain in effect until the water system ensures that chlorination can be adequately maintained and that, if necessary, any required corrections to structural systems or operational practices have been made. DEQ will require that proper testing of water samples indicates the water to be free from E. coli before suspending this advisory.
Federal law requires that consumers be notified when a public water supply exceeds certain maximum contaminant levels and might be harmful to the health of consumers.

COWLITZ COUNTY WATER SYSTEM OWNER FACES STIFF STATE FINE
States News Service
September 1, 2010 Wednesday


Copyright 2010 States News Service
Length: 358 words
Byline: States News Service
Dateline: OLYMPIA, WA
Body


The following information was released by the Washington State Department of Health:
The owner of the Columbia Crest Estates water system in Cowlitz County has been fined $21,060 for violating state health orders to properly maintain the water system and to address ongoing problems with arsenic.
Columbia Crest customers have been under a boil-water advisory since June 2 because owner Dan Class hasn't monitored water quality and doesn't have a certified operator to run the system, as the state requires. The state Department of Health issued the penalty after the failure of attempts to work with Class to address multiple system problems.
The agency's Office of Drinking Water inspected the system in July and found numerous sanitary issues, including mold, algae, and rodent infestations in buildings housing pumps, wells, and storage tanks. In addition, significant leaks pose a contamination risk.
The system serves 22 homes in an unincorporated area between Kalama and Woodland. The Department of Health has reclassified the system's operating permit as "red," which means the system is inadequate. This can affect decisions by local building officials and financial institutions about properties served by this water system.
Class did not comply with state health orders to:
- Hire a professional engineer and submit construction documents for an arsenic removal system to the Department of Health by May 15.
- Hire a certified water system operator by July 13 to run and maintain the system.
- Employ a professional engineer by July 20 to prepare a formal water system plan. These state-mandated plans require owners to demonstrate their technical, managerial and financial ability to maintain a safe and reliable water system.
"He has been given every chance to meet requirements designed to protect the health of his customers," said Clark Halvorson, manager of Southwest operations for the Office of Drinking Water. "We would much rather work cooperatively with water system operators and owners. Unfortunately, in this situation we've had to resort to a fine."
Class has 28 days to appeal the penalty to the agency's Adjudicative Service Unit.

BOIL WATER ADVISORY ISSUED FOR PRUDENCE ISLAND WATER DISTRICT
States News Service
September 3, 2010 Friday


Copyright 2010 States News Service
Length: 268 words
Byline: States News Service
Dateline: PROVIDENCE, RI
Body


The following information was released by the state of Rhode Island:
The Rhode Island Department of Health (HEALTH) has issued a boil water advisory for customers of the Prudence Island Water District (PIWD). HEALTH recommends that water used for bathing of infants, drinking, making ice, brushing teeth or cooking be boiled for one minute and allowed to cool before using. Boiling kills bacteria and other organisms in the water. Bottled water may also be used.
Water system tests confirmed the presence of E. Coli in the public water supply. PIWD is working closely with HEALTH to correct the problem as soon as possible.
The presence of E. Coli bacteria indicates that the water may be contaminated with human or animal wastes. These bacteria can cause diarrhea, cramps, nausea or headaches. Infants, young children, the elderly and anyone with a weakened immune system are at an increased risk for developing more severe symptoms. Consumers who experience any of these symptoms, even if tap water has been avoided, should call their healthcare provider.
This boil water advisory is in effect until further notice from HEALTH. Customers of the Prudence Island Water District are asked to contact neighbors who may not be aware of this advisory.
For information, contact the Prudence Island Water District at 401-835-0475. For general information about drinking water, contact HEALTH's Information Line at 401-222-5960, Monday - Friday, 8:30 a.m. - 4:30 p.m. For information on guidelines for food establishments during and after a boil water advisory, visit http://www.health.ri.gov/environment/dwq/boiladvisory.php

The following information was released by the Kansas Department of Health and Environment:
The Kansas Department of Health and Environment (KDHE) has issued a boil water advisory for the City of Norton, which is located in Norton County.
KDHE officials are issuing the advisory due to a break in a water main from the water treatment plant to town, which resulted in a loss of pressure and loss of water service in the distribution system. The water main is in the process of being repaired and whenever such a loss of pressure occurs, it is possible for contaminants to enter the system. Also during this time, disinfection (chlorine) residuals may drop to levels that are inadequate to protect against bacterial contamination.
Once water service is restored, residents in the City of Norton served by the affected public water system should observe the following precautions:
Boil water vigorously for one minute prior to use. Boiling longer than three minutes may adversely affect the quality and taste of the water.
Use only boiled water for drinking, brushing teeth, diluting fruit juices, and all other food preparation.
Dispose of ice cubes and do not use ice from a household automatic icemaker. Remake ice cubes with water that has been boiled.
Disinfect dishes and other food contact surfaces by immersion for at least one minute in clean tap water that contains one teaspoon of unscented household bleach per gallon of water.
Water used for bathing does not generally need to be boiled. Supervision of children is necessary while bathing or using backyard pools so water is not ingested. Persons with cuts or severe rashes may wish to consult their physicians.
The advisory will remain in effect until testing of water samples indicates no evidence of contamination and all other conditions which place the systems at risk of contamination are deemed by KDHE officials to be resolved. The city and/or KDHE will notify media when the boil water advisory has been rescinded.

Load-Date: September 10, 2010
END OF DOCUMENT

BOIL, WATER CONSERVATION ADVISORY ISSUED FOR CITY OF GLIDDEN
States News Service
September 19, 2010 Sunday


Copyright 2010 States News Service
Length: 289 words
Byline: States News Service
Dateline: GLIDDEN
Body


The following information was released by the Iowa Department of Natural Resources:
Residents in the Carroll County city of Glidden are being asked to boil and conserve water following a computer malfunction that caused the tower to drain Sunday afternoon.
Due to the potential for bacterial contamination, it is being recommended that the water be boiled before using for drinking or cooking or that an alternative source be used. The city is also asking that customers conserve water use. Due to the potential for bacterial contamination, residents are being urged to boil water before consuming, as well as conserving water as much as possible
By Sunday evening, the computer malfunction had been corrected and the tower was beginning to refill with water.
The boil and conservation advisory for Glidden will likely be in effect until at least Tuesday. Once the water tower has been completely refilled, pressure through the system restored and chlorine concentrations have been brought to an appropriate level, sampling will take place to make sure the water is safe and free of bacteria.
Glidden is working with the Iowa Department of Natural Resources to resolve the situation.
It is recommended not to drink the water without boiling it first. Bring all water to a boil, let it boil for one minute, and let it cool before using, or use bottled water. Boiled or bottled water should be used for drinking, making ice, brushing teeth, and food preparation until further notice. Boiling kills bacteria and other organisms in the water. The water may be used for bathing and other similar purposes.
General guidelines on ways to lessen the risk of infection by microbes are available from the EPA Safe Drinking Water Hotline at 1(800) 426-4791.

Load-Date: September 21, 2010
END OF DOCUMENT

Environment Department Issues "Boil Water Advisory" for Chippeway Water System in Otero County
Targeted News Service
September 21, 2010 Tuesday 1:06 AM EST


Copyright 2010 Targeted News Service LLC All Rights Reserved
Length: 314 words
Byline: Targeted News Service
Dateline: SANTA FE, N.M.
Body


The New Mexico Department of the Environment issued the following news release:
The New Mexico Environment Department's Drinking Water Bureau issued a "boil water advisory" for the Chippeway Water System.
NMED issued the advisory on today after bacteriological contamination (E. coli) was discovered in one of the drinking water sources for the system. NMED requires the system, located in Cox Canyon approximately 16 miles east of Alamogordo in Otero County, to notify water consumers of the finding.
This advisory only applies to the drinking water at the Chippeway Water System, and does not extend to any of the other surrounding water systems.
Consumers of the Cheppeway System are advised to boil the water for five minutes before drinking, cooking, dishwashing and bathing. The presence of E. coli in water indicates that the water may have been in contact with sewage or animal wastes, and could contain disease-causing organisms. Most strains of E. coli are harmless and live in the intestines of healthy humans and animals. However, a positive test for E. coli in the drinking water supply may indicate the presence of dangerous strains of E. coli or other disease-causing organisms. These types of organisms may cause severe gastrointestinal illness and, in rare cases, death. Children, the elderly and immuno-compromised individuals are at an increased risk for illness.
The NMED Drinking Water Bureau will provide technical assistance to the water system and will test the water until no further threat of contamination remains.
For more information, call NMED Communications Director Marissa Stone Bardino at (505) 827-0314 or (505) 231-0475 or Joe Savage, Drinking Water Bureau District IV Manager, at (575) 437-7115.
Contact: Marissa Stone Bardino, NMED Communications Director, 505/827-0314, 505/231-0475

Akron Debugging New Emergency Call System
Intelligencer Journal/New Era (Lancaster, Pennsylvania)
September 22, 2010 Wednesday


Copyright 2010 Lancaster Newspapers, Inc.
Section: B; Pg. 6
Length: 391 words
Byline: Kimberly Marselas, Correspondent
Dateline: Lancaster, PA
Body


BY KIMBERLY MARSELAS
Correspondent
Akron Borough is working out kinks in a new emergency notification system, following the first test of its automated calling program in August.
Several residents complained at a borough council meeting Sept. 13 that they were not contacted by the Swiftreach notification system when the borough issued a boil-water advisory on Aug. 12. One of the borough's wells tested positive for E. coli, and officials said about 80 percent of Akron's water customers were alerted to the problem by phone via the Swiftreach program.
But Council Vice President Terry Reber and Borough Manager Dan Guers acknowledged Sept. 13 that the system had problems reaching land lines with call blocking or answering machine services.
"The Swiftreach notification system is one that didn't exist for us six months ago," Reber said. "Until you use it in real-world conditions for the very first time, you don't know where the bugs are."
Officials asked those who were not contacted during the water emergency to call the borough or check the Akron Web site to update their contact information. Those who have disconnected landlines associated with their water accounts can provide a cell phone or e-mail addresses to be used by the system in the future.
Guers said the borough continued with all requirements to notify residents of the boil-water advisory, alerting the public through the media, fliers and the borough sign.
In other news, the borough's vacancy board appointed John Taylor of South Eight Street to fill the remainder of John Williamson's council term. Williamson resigned his seat last month to travel to Nepal for three years on behalf of the Mennonite Central Committee. Taylor, a truck sales specialist, has lived in Akron since 1990.
Council also approved a new ordinance establishing a boroughwide 25 mph speed limit. The new limit does not apply to Rothsville or North Farmersville roads, which will retain their 40 mph speed limits, or Seventh Street, which is posted at 35 mph. The private Lions Lane, which is the access lane to Loyd H. Roland Memorial Park, also will retain its 15 mph limit.
Council approved the speed change unanimously after months of consideration. Residents from several neighborhoods, particularly those near community parks, had complained that 35 mph limits were unreasonable and hard to enforce.

Load-Date: September 22, 2010
END OF DOCUMENT

Byline: Targeted News Service

Body


The New Mexico Department of the Environment issued the following news release:
The New Mexico Environment Department's Drinking Water Bureau advised the Estancia water system to issue a "boil water advisory" for its water system.
NMED issued the advisory on September 24th after bacteriological contamination that exceeded the Maximum Contaminant Level for E. coli was discovered in drinking water from the water system. NMED requires Estancia water system in Torrance County to notify its consumers of the finding.
Consumers of water from the Estancia water system are advised to boil water for five minutes before drinking, cooking and dishwashing or to use bottled water if at all possible.
The presence of E. coli in water indicates that the water may have been in contact with sewage or animal wastes, and could contain disease-causing organisms. Most strains of E. coli are harmless and live in the intestines of healthy humans and animals. However, a positive test for E. coli in the drinking water supply may indicate the presence of dangerous strains of E. coli or other disease-causing organisms, which are sometimes found in sewage or animal wastes. These types of organisms may cause severe gastrointestinal illness and, in rare cases, even death. Children, the elderly and immuno-compromised individuals are at an increased risk for illness.
Actions have been initiated to disinfect the water system and identify possible sources of contamination. The Drinking Water Bureau will continue to assist the water system and help identify the source of the problem.
For more information, call Marissa Stone Bardino at (505) 827-0314 or (505) 231-0475, Mike Huber at (505) 660-3834, or Joe Savage at (575) 258-3272 or (575) 973-0009.

Environment Department Lifts 'Boil Water Advisory' for Estancia Water System
Targeted News Service
September 27, 2010 Monday 2:44 AM EST


Copyright 2010 Targeted News Service LLC All Rights Reserved
Length: 243 words
Byline: Targeted News Service
Dateline: SANTA FE, N.M.
Body


The New Mexico Department of the Environment issued the following news release:
The New Mexico Environment Department's Drinking Water Bureau is lifting a "boil water advisory" for the Estancia Mutual Domestic Water Consumers Association Water System.
NMED issued the advisory on September 24, 2010 after bacteriological contamination that exceeded the Maximum Contaminant Level for E. coli was discovered in the water system. NMED required the Estancia Water System to notify all water consumers of the finding.
Corrective actions were taken by the water system, including disinfecting the water system by increasing the level of chlorination and identifying possible sources of contamination. Consumers were advised to boil all water prior to ingestion.
Water samples collected since the corrective actions were taken have shown no E. coli present in the distribution system. These clean distribution sample results and the protective levels of chlorine in the drinking water system have allowed NMED's Drinking Water Bureau to advise the Estancia Water System to lift the "boil water advisory" for the water system.
For more information, call NMED Communications Director Marissa Stone Bardino at (505) 827-0314 or (505) 231-0475 or Mike Huber, Drinking Water Bureau Compliance Manager, at (505) 476-8638.
Contact: Marissa Stone Bardino, NMED Communications Director, 505/827-0314, 505/231-0475

WATER ADVISORY ENDS FOR EAST KING COUNTY WATER SYSTEM
States News Service
September 27, 2010 Monday


Copyright 2010 States News Service
Length: 158 words
Byline: States News Service
Dateline: OLYMPIA, WA
Body


The following information was released by the Washington State Department of Health:
The boil-water advisory issued last Thursday for Riverbend Homesites in eastern King County ended today.
The state Department of Health issued the advisory as a precaution because E. coli bacteria were detected in routine monitoring samples. Since those initial tests, the water system operator took 11 more samples. All of the samples were good, indicating the water meets federal drinking water standards.
"Our priority is to ensure safe and reliable drinking water," said Bob James, manager of northwest operations for the agency's Office of Drinking Water. "We're pleased that the samples came back satisfactory, and we appreciate residents' understanding as we worked through this."
The Riverbend Homesites development has 533 homes and about 1,600 residents. It's near Interstate 90 Exit 32, east of North Bend. The advisory did not affect any other communities.

BOIL WATER ADVISORY ISSUED FOR THE CITY OF SEDAN

Byline: States News Service

Body


The following information was released by the Kansas Department of Health and Environment:
The Kansas Department of Health and Environment (KDHE) has issued a boil water advisory for the City of Sedan, which is located in Chautauqua County.
KDHE officials are issuing the advisory due to a number of water main breaks which were caused by water pressure changes after bringing a new water storage tank online. These main breaks have resulted in a loss of pressure and loss of water service in the distribution system. The water mains are in the process of being repaired and whenever such a loss of pressure occurs, it is possible for contaminants to enter the system. Also during this time, disinfection (chlorine) residuals may drop to levels that are inadequate to protect against bacterial contamination.
Once water service is restored, residents in the city of Sedan served by the affected public water system should observe the following precautions:
Boil water vigorously for one minute prior to use. Boiling longer than three minutes may adversely affect the quality and taste of the water.
Use only boiled water for drinking, brushing teeth, diluting fruit juices, and all other food preparation.
Dispose of ice cubes and do not use ice from a household automatic icemaker. Remake ice cubes with water that has been boiled.
Disinfect dishes and other food contact surfaces by immersion for at least one minute in clean tap water that contains one teaspoon of unscented household bleach per gallon of water.
Water used for bathing does not generally need to be boiled. Supervision of children is necessary while bathing or using backyard pools so water is not ingested. Persons with cuts or severe rashes may wish to consult their physicians.
The advisory will remain in effect until testing of water samples indicates no evidence of contamination and all other conditions which place the systems at risk of contamination are deemed by KDHE officials to be resolved. The City and/or KDHE will notify media when the boil water advisory has been rescinded. Concerned customers may contact the City by telephone at 620-725-3193.

Boil-water advisory issued for Trenton, 4 towns
The Associated Press State & Local Wire
October 4, 2010 Monday 9:30 PM GMT


Copyright 2010 Associated Press All Rights Reserved
Section: STATE AND REGIONAL
Length: 117 words
Dateline: TRENTON N.J.
Body


Residents of Trenton and four surrounding communities are being advised to boil water before drinking it.
That's because Trenton's water plant is having problems treating water due to the high level of the Delaware River.
In addition to the city of Trenton, residents of Ewing, Lawrence, Hopewell and Hamilton are being advised to boil water.
Officials said the heavy flow in the Delaware has forced them to draw from a water reservoir reserve. That's reduced volume of treated water to only one-quarter of the normal 28 million gallons per day as of Monday afternoon.
Officials did not know when the advisory would be lifted.
The Delaware is running higher than normal following last week's torrential rains.

BOIL WATER ADVISORY ISSUED FOR THE CITY OF ATCHISON
States News Service
October 6, 2010 Wednesday


Copyright 2010 States News Service
Length: 418 words
Byline: States News Service
Dateline: TOPEKA, KS
Body


The following information was released by the Kansas Department of Health and Environment:
The Kansas Department of Health and Environment (KDHE) has issued a boil water advisory for the City of Atchison, which is located in Atchison County.
KDHE officials are issuing the advisory due to a line break on the raw water line feeding the water treatment plant. Therefore, the City is unable to treat and produce drinking water which in turn has caused the distribution system to lose pressure and run dry. When a system loses pressure it is possible for contaminants to enter the system. Also during this time, disinfection (chlorine) residuals may drop to levels that are inadequate to protect against bacterial contamination.
The City of Atchison wholesales water to many consecutive systems. While the consecutive systems have not reported a loss of water service, they are espected to lose pressure and water service through the course of the day. As systems are affected, they should follow the boil water advisory. These systems include: Atchison County RWD 6, Atchison County RWD 1, Atchison County RWD 3, Atchison County RWD 5C, Doniphan County RWD 3 and the City of Lancaster.
Once water service is restored, residents in the City of Atchison and those affected by the above mentioned systems should observe the following precautions:
Boil water vigorously for one minute prior to use. Boiling longer than three minutes may adversely affect the quality and taste of the water.
Use only boiled water for drinking, brushing teeth, diluting fruit juices, and all other food preparation.
Dispose of ice cubes and do not use ice from a household automatic icemaker. Remake ice cubes with water that has been boiled.
Disinfect dishes and other food contact surfaces by immersion for at least one minute in clean tap water that contains one teaspoon of unscented household bleach per gallon of water.
Water used for bathing does not generally need to be boiled. Supervision of children is necessary while bathing or using backyard pools so water is not ingested. Persons with cuts or severe rashes may wish to consult their physicians.
The advisory will remain in effect until testing of water samples indicates no evidence of contamination and all other conditions which place the systems at risk of contamination are deemed by KDHE officials to be resolved. The City and/or KDHE will notify media when the boil water advisory has been rescinded. Concerned customers may contact the City by telephone at 913-367-5500.

Trenton city officials say tests on water in Lawrenceville and parts of Hopewell have come back clear. Tests are still pending in Trenton and Ewing and residents there are being told to continue to boil water before consuming it.
The boil-water advisory was issued Monday for five communities Trenton, Ewing, Hamilton, Lawrenceville and Hopewell because Trenton's water plant experienced problems treating water due to the high level of the Delaware River.
The water level in the Delaware is unusually high after last week's torrential rains.
Officials did not say when the advisory might be lifted for the remaining two communities.
State Sen. Senator Shirley Turner has asked the Environmental Protection Department for a full investigation into what led to water service disruptions in the Trenton area.
She expressed concern that the initial treatment plant shutdown occurred on Sunday but many residents of affected municipalities were not notified until late Monday of the potential water-quality threat.
The incident shuttered schools in the area, resulted in business interruptions and created panic among residents.

The city of Trenton issued the following news release:
Customers of Trenton Water Works in the City of Trenton, Ewing Township, Lawrence Township, and portions of Hopewell were notified on Monday, October 4, 2010 of a problem with the water due to a treatment plant shutdown on Sunday, October 3, 2010 which caused water outages and/or a significant loss of water pressure throughout our service area. Customers affected by this incident were advised to boil the water before using as precautionary measure.
We are pleased to report water service is PARTIALLY restored and subsequent water quality testing shows the water quality to be safe in Hopewell and Lawrence. The boil water advisory is partially lifted and it is no longer necessary to boil your water before using only in Hopewell and Lawrence.
The performance test results for Trenton and Ewing are not yet complete, and we expect to have these results from the state later this evening. Meanwhile residents of Trenton and Ewing are advised to continue to follow the precaution boil water advisory issued by the New Jersey Department of Environmental Protection.
The following measures are strongly encouraged at this time:
* Run your water faucets for 3-5 minutes to flush your service connection and interior plumbing with water from the service main.
* Empty and clean your automatic ice makers and water chillers.
* Drain and refill your hot water heater if the temperature is set below 113 degrees Fahrenheit.
* Service connections with a water softener/cartridge filters should be run through a regeneration cycle or other procedures recommended by the manufacturer.
* Water reservoirs in tall buildings should be drained and refilled.
We apologize for any inconvenience and thank you for your patience. If you have any questions or comments, please contact the Trenton Water Works at (609) 989-3208.
Contact: Lauren J. Ira, 609/989-3052

TRENTON BOIL WATER ADVISORY LIFTED; DEP AND CITY PLEDGE CLOSE COOPERATION TO ADDRESS TRENTON WATER ISSUES
States News Service
October 7, 2010 Thursday


Copyright 2010 States News Service
Length: 510 words
Byline: States News Service
Dateline: TRENTON, NJ
Body


The following information was released by the New Jersey Department of Environmental Protection (NJDEP):
In order to avoid future events like the severe loss of pressure that resulted in a precautionary boil water advisory for much of Trenton Water Works service area this week, DEP Commissioner Bob Martin announced that he and Trenton Mayor Tony Mack have pledged to work closely together to investigate this weeks events and to address the challenges facing the aging water utility.
Commissioner Martin today called Mayor Mack to offer the DEPs assistance in identifying and correcting any systemic, managerial or procedural problems at the Trenton Water Works. Both the Commissioner and the Mayor are determined to ascertain precisely how this weeks chain of events unfolded, and are committed to ensuring smooth operations in the future to protect public health. They are scheduled to meet Tuesday afternoon at the DEP.
Trenton Water Works, which is owned by the city, serves some 200,000 people in Trenton, Ewing, Hopewell, Lawrence and Hamilton. The utility is responsible for the treatment, delivery and testing of water, and for notification of its customers when a safety concern does arise.
While we are of course pleased that the loss of water pressure this week did not pose a health threat, Mayor Mack and I are concerned with how Trenton Water Works handled the situation, Commissioner Martin said. The Mayor has agreed to cooperate fully with the DEP and to correct any deficiencies that we identify. Mayor Mack and I share common goals: making sure that customers of Trenton Water Works receive a reliable supply of safe, high-quality drinking water.
Analyses of water tests confirmed that no bacteria contamination poses a threat to public health. As a result, the precautionary boil water advisory was lifted as of this afternoon for the entire Trenton Water Works service area except Ewing Township. The advisory for Ewing is expected to be lifted later tonight after completion of analysis of water samples from that community.
On Monday, the DEP ordered the utility to issue a boil water advisory as a precaution following low pressure in the system.
Preliminary information indicates that the utility temporarily closed off intakes from the Delaware River because of higher than normal flow in the river due to recent rains, but then had difficulty providing sufficient backup flow to meet demand. The utility was unable to provide sufficient flow from a reservoir that holds an emergency supply of treated water, resulting in significant and even complete loss of pressure in some parts of the system. The low pressure apparently caused corrosion in pipes to break loose, discoloring the water. The DEP does not believe that raw river water reached the distribution system at any time during the emergency.
I appreciated the phone call from Commissioner Martin today and am eager to work closely with the DEP to ensure that operations at Trenton Water Works provide a steady and safe supply of water to all of the utilitys customers, said Mayor Mack

Load-Date: October 8, 2010

Customers of the City of Toledo in Lewis County no longer have to boil their tap water. The water lines have been repaired, and lab test results received today show the city's tap water meets federal drinking water standards.
The advisory was issued Tuesday after a water line broke, causing a loss of water pressure. City crews shut down part of the water system in order to find the break and begin repairs. Loss of water pressure increases the risk that contaminated water could be drawn-in to the system.
This advisory affected nearly 400 homes and businesses served by the city water system, and involved several school closures. The state Department of Health worked closely with the city and local health officials throughout the incident.

Environment Department Lifts 'Boil Water Advisory' for El Vadito de Los Cerrillos Water Association Water System
Targeted News Service
October 12, 2010 Tuesday 1:31 AM EST


Copyright 2010 Targeted News Service LLC All Rights Reserved
Length: 409 words
Byline: Targeted News Service
Dateline: SANTA FE, N.M.
Body


The New Mexico Department of the Environment issued the following news release:
The New Mexico Environment Department's (NMED) Drinking Water Bureau has issued a "boil water advisory" for the El Vadito de Los Cerrillos Water Association Water System.
NMED issued the advisory on July 23, 2010 after bacteriological contamination that exceeded the Maximum Contaminant Level (MCL) for E. coli was discovered in drinking water at the water system. NMED requires the El Vadito de Los Cerrillos Water Association to notify water consumers of the finding. The El Vadito de Los Cerrillos Water Association Water System is located approximately 20 miles south of Santa Fe. This advisory only applied to customers served by the El Vadito de Los Cerrillos Water Association, and did not extend to any of the other surrounding water systems or communities.
Consumers of water at the El Vadito de Los Cerrillos Water Association Water System were advised to boil the water for five minutes before drinking, cooking, dishwashing and bathing. The presence of E. coli in water indicates that the water may have been in contact with sewage or animal wastes, and could contain disease-causing organisms. Most strains of E. coli are harmless and live in the intestines of healthy humans and animals. However, a positive test for E. coli in the drinking water supply may indicate the presence of dangerous strains of E. coli or other disease-causing organisms. These types of organisms may cause severe gastrointestinal illness and, in rare cases, death. Children, the elderly and immuno-compromised individuals are at an increased risk for illness.
The NMED Drinking Water Bureau provided technical assistance to the water system and determined that adequate disinfection (chlorination) is provided at a level that mitigates the potential threat to public health. The El Vadito de Los Cerrillos Water Association will maintain a regular monitoring schedule to ensure adequate levels of disinfection, and continue to test the distribution system for the presence of E. coli.
For more information, call NMED Communications Director Marissa Stone Bardino at (505) 827-0314 or (505) 231-0475 or Violette Valerio-Hirschfeld, New Mexico Environment Department, Drinking Water Bureau, District II Manager, at (505) 476-8636.
Contact: Marissa Stone Bardino, NMED Communications Director, 505/827-0314, 505/231-0475

DEP and City of Trenton Meet to Address Trenton Water Works Issues
Targeted News Service
October 13, 2010 Wednesday 3:04 AM EST


Copyright 2010 Targeted News Service LLC All Rights Reserved
Length: 419 words
Byline: Targeted News Service
Dateline: TRENTON, N.J.
Body


The New Jersey Department of Environmental Protection issued the following news release:
DEP Commissioner Bob Martin, Trenton Mayor Tony Mack and Trenton Water Works officials met yesterday afternoon at the DEP to discuss how to best tackle challenges faced by Trenton Water Works, as well as to examine events which led to last week's precautionary boil water advisory for much of the utility's service area, all in an effort to prevent future occurrences.
"I am pleased by the Mayor's eagerness to address concerns about the operations of the Trenton Water Works," said Commissioner Martin. "I want to emphasize again that the order for last week's boil water advisory was precautionary, that no untreated water left the plant, and that all of the tests showed the water was safe to drink. At the same time, Trenton Water Works must work not only to ensure continued high-quality drinking water but also to restore public confidence to its customers."
Last week, Trenton, Ewing, Lawrence, and parts of Hopewell west of Route 31 were under a precautionary boil water advisory due to a drop in water pressure; Trenton Water Works service is now fully restored.
After discussing the events of last week and identifying areas of Trenton Water Works operations that can be improved, Commissioner Martin and Mayor Mack agreed upon the following:
* Trenton Water Works will prepare a formal report to the DEP of last week's events by November 4;
* Another meeting date between the utility's staff and DEP water division staff is being set, at which time the Department will offer additional specific recommendations;
* The City of Trenton will secure an independent expert to conduct a thorough evaluation of the Trenton Water Works, including but not limited to operations, personnel, skills training, protocols;
* The City of Trenton will update its Emergency Response Plan and Trenton Water Works will update its Operations Plan to ensure clear and timely communications with municipalities and the public;
* DEP Assistant Commissioner John Plonski will oversee the Department's efforts to coordinate with Trenton Water Works.
"I appreciate that Commissioner Martin and the DEP water division staff have gone out of their way to offer their expertise and recommendations for Trenton Water Works. I am committed to working closely with the Commissioner to ensure best practices at Trenton Water Works," said Mayor Mack.
Contact: Lauren J. Ira, 609/989-3052

MASON COUNTY: POTLATCH BEACH MUTUAL CUSTOMERS URGED TO BOIL TAP WATER
States News Service
October 15, 2010 Friday


Copyright 2010 States News Service
Length: 363 words
Byline: States News Service
Dateline: OLYMPIA, WA
Body


The following information was released by the Washington State Department of Health:
The state Department of Health is advising customers of the Potlatch Beach Mutual Water System in north Mason County to boil their tap water or buy bottled water. E. coli has been detected in the water system.
The agency's Office of Drinking Water is working closely with Northwest Water Systems, the system's operator, to determine the source of the contamination. Boil-water notices were distributed today door-to-door to Potlatch Beach Mutual customers.
Two other water systems in the area - Minerva Terrace and Canal Mutual - also were placed under boil-water advisories earlier this week because of E. coli contamination. The three advisories collectively affect about 160 homes and businesses.
"While we can't say these advisories are directly related, we typically see more bacterial contamination problems caused by stormwater runoff this time of year," said Clark Halvorson, manager of Southwest regional operations for the Office of Drinking Water. "That's why we encourage small water systems and private well owners in this area to test their water at least monthly in the fall in order to detect problems more quickly and take action."
The Mason County Health Department is working with area food establishments to be sure they understand the order and follow the safety precautions needed for food preparation and water service.
The health advisory includes several precautionary steps customers should take: Use boiled water or bottled water for drinking, brushing teeth, preparing food, dishwashing, and making ice. Tap water should be boiled for one minute and allowed to cool before use.
The advisories will remain in effect until the state health agency and water system operators are satisfied there is no longer a health threat. Customers will be notified as the advisories end.
No illnesses have been reported in conjunction with this water contamination event.
Potlatch Beach Mutual water system customers who have questions can call Northwest Water Systems at 360-876-0958. Minerva Terrace and Canal Mutual customers can call Mason County Public Utility District 1 at 360-877-5249.

HEALTH ALERT: E. COLI DETECTED IN WESTERN HOOD CANAL WELLS PRIVATE WELL USERS, SMALL WATER SYSTEMS URGED TO TEST WELL WATER FOR BACTERIA
States News Service
October 20, 2010 Wednesday


Copyright 2010 States News Service
Length: 426 words
Byline: States News Service
Dateline: OLYMPIA, WA
Body


The following information was released by the Washington State Department of Health:
The state Department of Health urges Mason County well users along the western shore of Hood Canal to have their water tested. E. coli has been detected in the wells of three public water systems in the area over the past two weeks.
The contamination may have been caused by recent heavy rains. It's likely that more wells have been contaminated. Owners of all private wells and very small water systems (http://www.doh.wa.gov/ehp/dw/Publications/331-349.pdf), known as Group B systems, are strongly encouraged to have their water tested for coliform bacteria (   www.doh.wa.gov/ehp/dw/Programs/coliform.htm).
Older wells and poorly built wells are especially vulnerable to contamination.
The affected area is within 2,000 feet of the western shore of Hood Canal from the northern Mason County line south to the intersection of U.S. Highway 101 and State Route 106.
"It's very rare to find E. coli in several wells at the same time," said Clark Halvorson, manager of southwest regional operations for the Department of Health's Office of Drinking Water. "Our staff believes runoff from the unusually heavy rains early this month allowed contaminated water to seep into the water table, which may have contributed to some of the problems."
Well users and water systems can call Mason County Health Department at 360-427-9670 (ext. 400) for information about where to pick up and drop off sample water bottles. More information is on the Mason County website (www.co.mason.wa.us/health/envhealth/water_lab/index.php), the Department of Health's website (   www.doh.wa.gov/ehp/dw/Publications/331-242_4-21-06.pdf), and the Department of Ecology website (   www.ecy.wa.gov/programs/eap/labs/documents/DWLabsScopesInternet.pdf).
The three Mason County water systems currently under boil water advisories are Potlatch Beach Mutual, Canal Mutual, and Minerva Terrace. The three advisories collectively affect about 160 homes and businesses.
The health advisories include several precautionary steps customers should take: Use boiled water or bottled water for drinking, brushing teeth, preparing food, dishwashing, and making ice. Tap water should be brought to a rolling boil for one minute and allowed to cool before use.
The advisories will remain in effect until the state health department and water system operators are satisfied there is no longer a health threat. Customers will be notified as the advisories end.
There have been no reports of illness from users of the three water systems.

BOIL WATER ADVISORY ISSUED FOR THE CITY OF CANTON
States News Service
October 22, 2010 Friday


Copyright 2010 States News Service
Length: 367 words
Byline: States News Service
Dateline: TOPEKA, KS
Body


The following information was released by the Kansas Department of Health and Environment:
The Kansas Department of Health and Environment (KDHE) has issued a boil water advisory for the City of Canton, which is located in eastern McPherson County.
KDHE officials are issuing the advisory in advance of work to begin at 2 p.m. on Friday, October 22. The City will shut down water production in order to make repairs and conduct work on the storage tank and valves in the distribution system. During this time, customers will lose pressure and be without water service until work is completed. Whenever such a loss of pressure occurs, it is possible for contaminants to enter the system. Also during this time, disinfection (chlorine) residuals may drop to levels that are inadequate to protect against bacterial contamination.
The City anticipates work to be completed late Friday evening. Once water service is restored, residents in the city of Canton served by the affected public water system should observe the following precautions:
Boil water vigorously for one minute prior to use. Boiling longer than three minutes may adversely affect the quality and taste of the water.
Use only boiled water for drinking, brushing teeth, diluting fruit juices, and all other food preparation.
Dispose of ice cubes and do not use ice from a household automatic icemaker. Remake ice cubes with water that has been boiled.
Disinfect dishes and other food contact surfaces by immersion for at least one minute in clean tap water that contains one teaspoon of unscented household bleach per gallon of water.
Water used for bathing does not generally need to be boiled. Supervision of children is necessary while bathing or using backyard pools so water is not ingested. Persons with cuts or severe rashes may wish to consult their physicians.
The advisory will remain in effect until testing of water samples indicates no evidence of contamination and all other conditions which place the systems at risk of contamination are deemed by KDHE officials to be resolved. The City and/or KDHE will notify media when the boil water advisory has been rescinded. Concerned customers may contact the City by telephone at 620-628-4916.

Tajique avoids sale of its water system
The Independent (Edgewood, New Mexico)
October 27, 2010


Copyright 2010 SmallTownPapers, Inc.
All Rights Reserved
SmallTownPapers, Inc.
Copyright 2010 The Independent


This content, including derivations, may not be stored or distributed in any manner, disseminated, published, broadcast, rewritten or reproduced without express, written consent from STPNS
Length: 259 words
Byline: The Independent staff
Body


The Tajique Mutual Domestic Water Consumers Association borrowed $40,355 from the state last week to avoid a court judgment putting the water association up for sale.
Barb Christy, vice president of the association said, "The amount was unavailable for payment until Oct. 14, a day before the system was to be sold."
Members of the water system voted to double their monthly water rates from $20 to $40 to pay back the loan.
The association made an agreement with Frank and Loretta Dow in 2002 to drill a well west of the community, Christy said.
"The Dows did not feel the work was done according to the agreement and took the association to court on more than one occasion, and judgment was in their favor," Christy said. "We all wanted this resolved, and I am glad the problem is behind us.
Everyone needs water, and we were responsible to pay the amount."
In April the state Environment Department's Drinking Water Bureau issued a boil water advisory for the water systems in both Tajique and Punta de Agua.
According to a press release, both were cited for multiple failures to test for bacteria and to meet sampling and reporting requirements. No indications of contamination were found at either site, and the boil water advisories were lifted when samples were completed.
"We have that under control now," Christy said.
The community water system was first created in 1948 and now has 60 hook-ups, she said. "Our current well is absolutely excellent. It pumps approximately 35 gallons a minute and provides good pressure for water consumers in the community."

Load-Date: August 13, 2011

The Oklahoma Department of Environmental Quality issued the following news release:
The Oklahoma Department of Environmental Quality (DEQ) has announced that follow-up water samples submitted by Applewood Mobile Home Park in Oklahoma City indicate the water is free from bacteria, there is adequate chlorine residual for disinfection throughout the system, and the water is now safe for human consumption. The boil order for Applewood has been lifted.
The advisory to boil water intended for drinking or cooking was issued after initial and follow-up water samples submitted for routine analysis indicated the presence of E. coli.
State and federal regulations require that customers be notified if, at any time, public drinking water is determined to be unsafe.
DEQ is responsible for regulating more than 1,600 public water supplies in the State of Oklahoma. All public water supplies are required to regularly submit samples to DEQ for routine testing to ensure that water is safe for human consumption.

MASON COUNTY: BOIL-WATER ADVISORY ENDS FOR POTLATCH BEACH MUTUAL
States News Service
November 8, 2010 Monday


Copyright 2010 States News Service
Length: 249 words
Byline: States News Service
Dateline: OLYMPIA, WA
Body


The following information was released by the Washington State Department of Health:
Customers of the Potlatch Beach Mutual Water System in north Mason County no longer need to boil their tap water. The water system and its well have been disinfected, and the water now meets federal drinking water standards.
Two nearby water systems - Minerva Terrace and Canal Mutual - remain under boil-water advisories. E. coli was found in the wells of all three water systems last month. E. coli also has been confirmed in at least one private well in the area.
The state Department of Health encourages Minerva Terrace and Canal Mutual customers to continue boiling their tap water until they're told the danger has passed. In addition, the agency urges private well users and very small water systems in the area to have their water tested now for coliform bacteria if they haven't already. They can call Mason County Health Department at 360-427-9670, extension 400, for information about where to pick up and drop off sampling bottles.
Unusually heavy rains in early October are likely to blame for the contamination. Older wells and poorly built wells are especially vulnerable to contamination from water runoff. No illnesses have been reported in connection with this water contamination event.
Potlatch Beach Mutual customers who have questions can call Northwest Water Systems at 360-876-0958. Minerva Terrace and Canal Mutual customers can call Mason County Public Utility District 1 at 360-877-5249.

MASON COUNTY: TIMBERLAKE COMMUNITY CLUB RESIDENTS ADVISED TO BOIL WATER
States News Service
November 10, 2010 Wednesday


Copyright 2010 States News Service
Length: 239 words
Byline: States News Service
Dateline: OLYMPIA, WA
Body


The following information was released by the Washington State Department of Health:
Residents of the Timberlake Community Club in southeastern Mason County are advised to boil their water following a water outage.
A broken pipe that drained the water reservoir caused the outage. Water lines lost pressure, which may have allowed contaminants to get into the system.
Timberlake Community Club is a residential area located on Agate Road about five miles east of Shelton. The community's water system serves about 800 homes.
The water system staff has repaired the broken pipe, and will flush water lines as soon as the reservoir has refilled. Workers are collecting water samples to test for coliform bacteria. Lab tests take a minimum of 24 hours to complete. The boil-water advisory will remain in effect until tests show the water meets safe drinking standards.
In the meantime, community club managers are providing bottled water to residents. The state Department of Health advises those who choose to use tap water for drinking, brushing teeth, dishwashing, preparing food, and making ice to boil the water first. Water should be boiled for one minute and allowed to cool before use.
"I'm pleased with how well the water system responded to this situation," said Clark Halvorson, manager of southwest regional operations for the agency's Office of Drinking Water.
Residents who have questions about the advisory can call 360-427-8928.

East Bank of Orleans Parish Under Precautionary Boil Water Advisory Until Sunday Afternoon
Targeted News Service
November 20, 2010 Saturday 2:29 AM EST


Copyright 2010 Targeted News Service LLC All Rights Reserved
Length: 555 words
Byline: Targeted News Service
Dateline: NEW ORLEANS
Body


The city of New Orleans issued the following news release:
Mayor Landrieu, Public Health officials, and Sewerage & Water Board officials addressed the media today to update citizens on the precautionary Boil Water Advisory issued for the East Bank of Orleans Parish. The precautionary Boil Water Advisory is expected to be in place until Sunday afternoon at approximately 3:00 pm, when water test results can be verified by the state Department of Health and Hospitals. This does not affect the West Bank.
"I want to stress that this is a precautionary measure and the City is following the protocol required by the state sanitary code," said Mayor Mitch Landrieu. "Based on our conversations with health officials and the Sewerage and Water Board, we are confident that the risk is low."
The State recommends that you disinfect your water by boiling it for one minute and letting it cool down prior to consumption (including drinking, cooking, brushing teeth, bathing or preparing food). Boil water for one full minute in a clean container. The one-minute boil time begins after the water has been brought to a rolling boil. (If there is a flat taste, it can be eliminated by shaking the water in a bottle or pouring it from one container to another.)
"We're uncertain at this point if there was a compromise to the system," said Dr. Takeisha Davis, Regional Medical Director at the Louisiana Office of Public Health. "The major risk is from ingestion, and we think that this risk is very low."
Davis added, "There is little risk to taking a shower, as long as individuals close their mouths and do not ingest the water. However, we recommend that individuals with open wounds or immune system deficiencies take special precautions and avoid showering while the precautionary boil advisory is in effect."
At approximately 7:00 am on Saturday, the Sewerage and Water Board's chemists and technicians began collecting 28 water samples from sites throughout the East Bank. Analysis began at 12:00 PM of all samples. Tests are being conducted at the Board's Water Purification Laboratory. Tests will be incubated for 24 hours to determine if any harmful bacteria are present in the samples. If the tests show that the water is free of harmful bacteria and has a normal chlorine concentration, the precautionary Boil Water Advisory would then be lifted with the approval of the Department of Health and Hospitals (DHH).
At approximately 10:30 pm on Friday, the Sewerage & Water Board lost 25 cycle power at its main water plant, causing low water pressure (as low as 10 pounds per square inch) throughout the East Bank of the City. The Board has restored its 25-cycle power and is also operating on commercial power. According to the Board, water pressure has approached near-normal pressure, as repairs to the electrical system at the main water plant are underway. The Mayor has ordered an after action report to determine what caused the power failure.
The City's Office of Homeland Security and the State Department of Health and Hospitals are in contact with hospital, hotel, restaurant, and tourism officials to help ensure continuity of operations.
For information, citizens can log onto www.nola.gov or   www.swbno.org. Citizens can call 311 (and press zero) or 658-4000.

Much of New Orleans is under a boil-water advisory until at least Sunday afternoon, Mayor Mitch Landrieu said Saturday.

Precautionary Boil Water Advisory Cancelled
Targeted News Service
November 21, 2010 Sunday 2:19 AM EST


Copyright 2010 Targeted News Service LLC All Rights Reserved
Length: 286 words
Byline: Targeted News Service
Dateline: NEW ORLEANS
Body


The city of New Orleans issued the following news release:
Mayor Landrieu, public health officials, and Sewerage &
Water Board officials announced this evening that the precautionary Boil Water Advisory issued for the East Bank of Orleans Parish yesterday has been cancelled. Test results were verified by the state Department of Health and Hospitals.
"After following the protocols of the federal Environmental Protection Agency and the state Department of Health and Hospitals, and after working with doctors, engineers, chemists and other experts, we can report that the water in New Orleans is safe and the precautionary Boil Water Advisory is cancelled," said Mayor Mitch Landrieu.
State health regulations required the precautionary Boil Water Advisory and testing because water pressure dropped below 15 psi (pounds per square inch) which increases the risk of contaminants entering the water system.
At approximately 7:00 am on Saturday, the Sewerage and Water Board's chemists and technicians began collecting 28 water samples from sites throughout the East Bank. In an abundance of caution, a second round of sampling began at 2:00 pm Saturday. Tests were conducted at the Board's Water Purification Laboratory. A 24-hour incubation period is required to determine if any harmful bacteria are present in the samples.
At approximately 10:30 pm on Friday, the Sewerage & Water Board lost 25-cycle power at its main water plant, causing low water pressure (as low as 10 pounds per square inch) throughout the East Bank of the City. According to the Board, water pressure has normalized.
The Mayor has ordered an after action report of the incident.
